3416</section>

3417<section id="_595">

3418<h4 id="_595_toc">

3419Surgery before or after platinum-based chemotherapy and/or additional consolidation therapy</h4>

3420<p id="_757" tabindex="-1">

3421The pharmacological basis for the delivery of anticancer drugs by the IP route was established in the late 1970s and early 1980s. When several drugs were studied, mostly in the setting of measurable residual disease at reassessment after patients had received their initial chemotherapy, cisplatin alone and in combination received the most attention. Favorable outcomes from IP cisplatin were most often seen when tumors had shown responsiveness to platinum therapy and with small-volume tumors (usually defined as tumors &lt;1 cm).[<a href="#cit/section_6.34">

342234</a>

3423] </p>

3424<p id="_856" tabindex="-1">

3425In the 1990s, randomized trials were conducted to evaluate whether the IP route would prove superior to the IV route. IP cisplatin was the common denominator of these randomized trials. </p>

3426<p id="_982" tabindex="-1">

3427Evidence (surgery followed by IP chemotherapy):</p>

3428<div class="pdq-content-list">

3429<ol id="_983">

3430<li>

3431The use of IP cisplatin as part of the initial approach in patients with stage III optimally debulked ovarian cancer is supported principally by the results of three randomized clinical trials (SWOG-8501, GOG-0114, and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00003322">

3432GOG-0172</a>

3433 [NCT00003322]).[<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

34348</a>

3435,<a href="#cit/section_6.35">

343635</a>

3437,<a href="#cit/section_6.36">

343836</a>

3439] These studies tested the role of IP drugs (IP cisplatin in all three studies and IP paclitaxel in the last study) against the standard IV regimen.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3440<ul id="_984">

3441<li>

3442In the three studies, superior PFS and OS favoring the IP arm were documented.</li>

3443</ul>

3444</div>

3445<p id="_985" tabindex="-1">

3446Specifically, the most recent study, <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00003322">

3447GOG-0172</a>

3448, demonstrated the following:[<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

34498</a>

3450][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3451Level of evidence A1</a>

3452]</p>

3453<div class="pdq-content-list">

3454<ul id="_986">

3455<li>

3456A median survival of 66 months for patients on the IP arm versus 50 months for patients who received IV administration of cisplatin and paclitaxel (<em>

3457P</em>

3458 = .03).</li>

3459<li>

3460Toxic effects were greater in the IP arm because of the cisplatin dose per cycle (100 mg/m<span class="sup">

34612</span>

3462); sensory neuropathy resulted from the additional IP chemotherapy and from the systemic administration of paclitaxel.</li>

3463<li>

3464The rate of completion of six cycles of treatment was also less frequent in the IP arm (42% vs. 83%) because of the toxic effects and catheter-related problems.</li>

3465</ul>

3466</div>

3467<p id="_987" tabindex="-1">

3468An updated combined analysis of GOG-0114 and GOG-0172 included 876 patients with a median follow-up of 10.7 years and reported the following results.[<a href="#cit/section_6.37">

346937</a>

3470]</p>

3471<div class="pdq-content-list">

3472<ul id="_968">

3473<li>

3474Median survival with IP therapy was 61.8 months (95% CI, 55.5&#8211;69.5) compared with 51.4 months (95% CI, 46.0&#8211;58.2) for IV therapy.</li>

3475<li>

3476IP therapy was associated with a 23% decreased risk of death (adjusted hazard ratio [AHR], 0.77; 95% CI, 0.65&#8211;0.90; <em>

3477P</em>

3478 = .002). </li>

3479<li>

3480IP therapy improved the survival of patients with gross residual (&#8804;1 cm) disease (AHR, 0.75; 95% CI, 0.62&#8211;0.92; <em>

3481P</em>

3482 = .006). </li>

3483<li>

3484Risk of death decreased by 12% for each cycle of IP chemotherapy completed (AHR, 0.88; 95% CI, 0.83&#8211;0.94; <em>

3485P</em>

3486 &lt; .001). </li>

3487<li>

3488Factors associated with poorer survival included clear and mucinous versus serous histology (AHR, 2.79; 95% CI, 1.83&#8211;4.24; <em>

3489P</em>

3490 &lt; .001), gross residual versus no visible disease (AHR, 1.89; 95% CI, 1.48&#8211;2.43; <em>

3491P</em>

3492 &lt; .001), and fewer versus more cycles of IP chemotherapy (AHR, 0.88; 95% CI, 0.83&#8211;0.94; <em>

3493P</em>

3494 &lt; .001). </li>

3495<li>

3496Younger patients were more likely to complete the IP regimen, with a 5% decrease in probability of completion with each year of age (odds ratio, 0.95; 95% CI, 0.93&#8211;0.96; <em>

3497P</em>

3498 &lt; .001). </li>

3499</ul>

3500</div>

3501</li>

3502<li>

3503A Cochrane-sponsored meta-analysis of all randomized IP-versus-IV trials showed an HR of 0.79 for disease-free survival and 0.79 for OS, favoring the IP arms.[<a href="#cit/section_6.38">

350438</a>

3505]</li>

3506<li>

3507In another meta-analysis of seven randomized trials assessing IP versus systemic chemotherapy conducted by Cancer Care of Ontario, the relative ratio (RR) of disease progression at 5 years based on the three trials that reported this end point was 0.91 (95% CI, 0.85&#8211;0.98), and the RR of death at 5 years based on six trials was 0.88 (95% CI, 0.81&#8211;0.95) for the IP route.[<a href="#cit/section_6.39">

350839</a>

3509]</li>

3510<li>

3511In the subsequent IP trial (GOG-252), modifications of the IP regimen used in GOG-0172 were made to improve its tolerability (e.g., to reduce by &#8805;25% the total 3-hour amount of cisplatin given; and, to shift from the less practical 24-hour IV administration of paclitaxel to a 3-hour IV administration).[<a href="#cit/section_6.40">

351240</a>

3513]<p id="_1400" tabindex="-1">

3514In this study, 1,560 patients were randomly assigned to receive six cycles of IV paclitaxel (80 mg/m<span class="sup">

35152</span>

3516 once per week with IV carboplatin [AUC, 6] every 3 weeks) versus IV paclitaxel (80 mg/m<span class="sup">

35172</span>

3518 once per week with IP carboplatin [AUC, 6] [the IP carboplatin arm]) versus once-every-3-weeks IV paclitaxel (135 mg/m<span class="sup">

35192</span>

3520 over 3 hours on day 1, IP cisplatin 75 mg/m<span class="sup">

35212</span>

3522 on day 2, and IP paclitaxel 60 mg/m<span class="sup">

35232</span>

3524 on day 8 [the IP cisplatin arm]). The last regimen was the modified IP superior arm of GOG-0172. All participants received bevacizumab (15 mg/kg IV every 3 weeks in cycles 2&#8722;22) and bevacizumab (15 mg/kg every 3 weeks) was added to all three arms. </p>

3525<div class="pdq-content-list">

3526<ul id="_1401">

3527<li>

3528The median PFS duration was 24.9 months in the IV carboplatin arm, 27.4 months in the IP carboplatin arm, and 26.2 months in the IP cisplatin arm. </li>

3529<li>

3530For the subgroup of 1,380 patients with stage II/III and residual disease of 1 cm or less, the median PFS was 26.9 months in the IV carboplatin arm, 28.7 months in the IP carboplatin arm, and 27.8 months in the IP cisplatin arm. </li>

3531<li>

3532The median PFS for patients with stage II/III disease and no residual tumor was 35.9, 38.8, and 35.5 months, respectively. </li>

3533<li>

3534The median OS for all enrolled patients was 75.5, 78.9, and 72.9 months, respectively; the median OS for patients with stage II/III disease with no gross residual tumor was 98.8 months, 104.8 months, and not reached, respectively.</li>

3535<li>

3536This study concluded that, compared with the IV carboplatin reference arm, PFS was not significantly increased with either IP regimen when combined with bevacizumab.[<a href="#cit/section_6.40">

353740</a>

3538][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3539Level of evidence B1</a>

3540] </li>

3541</ul>

3542</div>

3543</li>

3544</ol>

3545</div>

3546</section>

3547<section id="_692">

3548<h4 id="_692_toc">

3549Surgery before or after platinum-based chemotherapy and the addition of bevacizumab to induction and/or consolidation therapy</h4>

3550<p id="_1016" tabindex="-1">

3551Two phase III studies compared the outcome of standard primary cytoreductive surgery with that of neoadjuvant chemotherapy followed by interval cytoreductive surgery; both studies (described below) demonstrated that PFS and OS were noninferior with the use of primary cytoreductive surgery.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

355241</a>

3553,<a href="#cit/section_6.42">

355442</a>

3555]</p>

3556<p id="_939" tabindex="-1">

3557Evidence (chemotherapy followed by surgery):</p>

3558<div class="pdq-content-list">

3559<ol id="_899">

3560<li>

3561Between 1998 and 2006, a study led by the European Organisation for the Research and Treatment of Cancer (EORTC) Gynecological Cancer Group, together with the National Cancer Institute of Canada Clinical Trials Group (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00003636">

3562EORTC-55971</a>

3563 [NCT00003636]), included 670 women with stages IIIC and IV ovarian epithelial cancer, FTC, and PPC.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

356441</a>

3565][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3566Level of evidence A1</a>

3567] The women were randomly assigned to undergo primary debulking surgery followed by at least six courses of platinum-based chemotherapy or to receive three courses of neoadjuvant platinum-based chemotherapy followed by interval debulking surgery, and at least three more courses of platinum-based chemotherapy. <p id="_950" tabindex="-1">

3568Methods included efforts to ensure accuracy of diagnosis (e.g., rule out peritoneal carcinomatosis of gastrointestinal origin) and stratification by largest preoperative tumor size (excluding ovaries) (&lt;5 cm, &gt;5 cm&#8211;10 cm, &gt;10 cm&#8211;20 cm, or &gt;20 cm). Other stratification factors included institution, method of biopsy (i.e., image-guided, laparoscopy, laparotomy, or fine-needle aspiration), and tumor stage (i.e., stage IIIC or IV). The primary end point of the study was OS, with primary debulking surgery considered the standard.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

356941</a>

3570][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3571Level of evidence A1</a>

3572]</p>

3573<div class="pdq-content-list">

3574<ul id="_900">

3575<li>

3576Median OS for primary debulking surgery was 29 months, compared with 30 months for patients assigned to neoadjuvant chemotherapy. </li>

3577<li>

3578The HR<sub>

3579death</sub>

3580 in the group assigned to neoadjuvant chemotherapy followed by interval debulking, as compared with the group assigned to primary debulking surgery followed by chemotherapy, was 0.98 (90% CI, 0.84&#8211;1.13; <em>

3581P</em>

3582 = .01 for noninferiority).[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

358341</a>

3584][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3585Level of evidence A1</a>

3586]</li>

3587<li>

3588 Perioperative and postoperative morbidity and mortality were higher in the primary debulking surgery group (7.4% severe hemorrhage and 2.5% deaths, compared with 4.1% severe hemorrhage and 0.7% deaths in the neoadjuvant group). </li>

3589<li>

3590The strongest independent predictor of prolonged survival was the absence of residual tumor after surgery. </li>

3591<li>

3592The subset of patients achieving optimal cytoreduction (&#8804;1 cm residuum), whether after primary debulking surgery or after neoadjuvant chemotherapy followed by interval debulking surgery, had the best median OS.</li>

3593</ul>

3594</div>

3595</li>

3596<li>

3597Between 2004 and 2010, a group of 87 hospitals in the United Kingdom and New Zealand enrolled 550 women with stage III or IV ovarian epithelial cancer and randomly assigned them to undergo primary cytoreductive surgery followed by six cycles of chemotherapy or primary (neoadjuvant) chemotherapy for three cycles, followed by surgery and three additional cycles of chemotherapy. In contrast to the EORTC study, the chemotherapy consisted of conventional carboplatin (AUC, 5 or AUC, 6) and paclitaxel (175 mg/m<span class="sup">

35982</span>

3599, in 76% of patients), or carboplatin alone (23% of patients), or nonpaclitaxel chemotherapy (1% of patients).[<a href="#cit/section_6.42">

360042</a>

3601][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3602Level of evidence A1</a>

3603]<p id="_1122" tabindex="-1">

3604A minimization method was used to randomly assign patients in a 1:1 ratio.[<a href="#cit/section_6.43">

360543</a>

3606] Participants were stratified by randomizing center, largest radiological tumor, and prespecified chemotherapy regimen. The primary end point was to establish noninferiority, with the upper bound of a one-sided 90% CI for the HR<sub>

3607death</sub>

3608 at less than 1.18.</p>

3609<div class="pdq-content-list">

3610<ul id="_1017">

3611<li>

3612As of May 2014, 451 deaths had occurred, and the HR<sub>

3613death</sub>

3614 favored neoadjuvant chemotherapy, with the upper bound of the one-sided 90% CI of 0.98 (95% CI, 0.72&#8210;1.05).</li>

3615<li>

3616The most common grade 3 or 4 postoperative adverse event was hemorrhage in both groups, with 8 women (3%) having this problem with primary cytoreductive surgery versus 14 (6%) in the neoadjuvant chemotherapy group. Grade 3 and 4 toxic events from chemotherapy occurred in 110 (49%) of 225 women randomly assigned to primary cytoreductive surgery and in 102 (40%) of the 253 women receiving neoadjuvant chemotherapy, with one fatal event of neutropenic sepsis occurring in the primary chemotherapy group. </li>

3617</ul>

3618</div>

3619</li>

3620</ol>

3621</div>

3622<p id="_1018" tabindex="-1">

3623These studies and additional observational and partially published phase III studies have led to the publication of a Clinical Practice Guideline on behalf of the Society of Gynecologic Oncology and the American Society of Clinical Oncology.[<a href="#cit/section_6.44">

362444</a>

3625]</p>

3626<p id="_1402" tabindex="-1">

3627Hyperthermic peritoneal chemotherapy (HIPEC) is another pharmacologically based modality to enhance the antitumor effects via direct drug delivery to peritoneal surfaces.

3628It was initially tested against mucinous tumors of gastrointestinal origin.[<a href="#cit/section_6.45">

362945</a>

3630]

3631Increasingly, HIPEC is being applied to ovarian cancers, with considerable variation in patient selection, drugs administered, and time at target temperatures (most often 30 minutes at 42&#176;C).

3632The role of HIPEC remains experimental in the treatment of patients with high-grade serous ovarian cancers.</p>

3633<p id="_1107" tabindex="-1">

3634Experience with HIPEC spans more than two decades after initial publications that have since been summarized.[<a href="#cit/section_6.46">

363546</a>

3636] Evidence for its use in ovarian cancer includes a randomized study.</p>

3637<div class="pdq-content-list">

3638<ol id="_1108">

3639<li>

3640The final results of a phase III, open-label Dutch study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00426257">

3641NCT00426257</a>

3642) have been published. The study was performed in eight hospitals and included 245 patients with newly diagnosed ovarian cancer who were at least stable after receiving three cycles of carboplatin (AUC, 5&#8211;6) and paclitaxel 175 mg/m<span class="sup">

36432</span>

3644, both of which were given by IV every 3 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_6.47">

364547</a>

3646] Randomization took place at the time of surgery, and patients were assigned to undergo either cytoreductive surgery without HIPEC (n = 123) or with HIPEC (n = 122). All patients subsequently received three additional cycles of IV chemotherapy. The study was reported with a median follow-up of 4.7 years, after the surgical intervention. HIPEC consisted of perfusion of the abdominal cavity with cisplatin 100 mg/m<span class="sup">

36472</span>

3648 in heated saline at 40&#176;C (104&#176;F) that was maintained for 60 minutes. Sodium thiosulfate was given at the start of the perfusion as an IV bolus of 9 g/m<span class="sup">

36492</span>

3650 in 200 mL followed by continuous infusion IV (12 g/m<span class="sup">

36512</span>

3652 in 1L) for 6 hours.[<a href="#cit/section_6.48">

365348</a>

3654]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3655<ul id="_1109">

3656<li>

3657After a median follow-up of 4.7 years, 209 of the 245 patients had a recurring disease event or died. In an intention-to-treat analysis, 110 of 123 patients in the surgery group and 99 of 122 patients in the HIPEC group had such an event (HR, 0.66; 95% CI, 0.50&#8211;0.87; <em>

3658P</em>

3659 = .003).</li>

3660<li>

3661The median recurrence-free survival was 3.5 months longer in the HIPEC group (14.2 months vs. 10.7 months). </li>

3662<li>

3663 In the surgery group, 76 of 123 patients (62%) had died, but in the HIPEC group, 61 of 122 patients (50%) had died at the time of publication (HR, 0.67; 95% CI, 0.48&#8211;0.94; <em>

3664P</em>

3665 = .02) with median OS of 33.9 months in the surgery group and 45.7 months in the HIPEC group. </li>

3666<li>

3667In the two groups, patient characteristics were mostly balanced with regard to age (median age, 61 years in both groups), histological cell type in patients with high-grade serous ovarian carcinoma (87% in the surgery group and 92% in the HIPEC group), residual disease after surgery, and the number of patients completing adjuvant chemotherapy after surgery (90% in the surgery group and 94% in the HIPEC group).</li>

3668</ul>

3669</div>

3670</li>

3671</ol>

3672</div>

3673<p id="_1110" tabindex="-1">

3674 In the institutions that have experience performing HIPEC, adverse events were comparable in the two groups. Patients in the HIPEC group had higher incidences of ileus (3% vs. 8%), fever (8% vs. 12%), and thromboembolic events (2% vs. 6%), but in that group, there were smaller differences in electrolyte changes (5% vs. 6%) and neuropathy (27% vs. 31%) than in patients in the surgery group, and both groups of patients had added IV chemotherapy. The use of sodium thiosulfate most likely accounts for this favorable safety profile vis-&#224;-vis cisplatin, which was given as part of HIPEC in a published phase I trial.[<a href="#cit/section_6.49">

367549</a>

3676] HIPEC should be considered an option for patients who receive neoadjuvant therapy if they have access to a surgical team who has experience performing HIPEC.</p>

3677<p id="_760" tabindex="-1">

3678Two phase III trials (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00262847">

3679GOG-0218</a>

3680 [NCT00262847] and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00483782">

3681ICON7 </a>

3682 [NCT00483782]) have evaluated the role of bevacizumab in first-line therapy for ovarian epithelial cancer, FTC, and PPC after surgical cytoreduction.[<a href="#cit/section_6.50">

368350</a>

3684,<a href="#cit/section_6.51">

368551</a>

3686] Both trials showed a modest improvement in PFS when bevacizumab was added to initial chemotherapy and continued every 3 weeks for 16 and 12 additional cycles, as a maintenance phase. </p>

3687<p id="_880" tabindex="-1">

3688Evidence (surgery followed by chemotherapy and bevacizumab):</p>

3689<div class="pdq-content-list">

3690<ol id="_862">

3691<li>

3692GOG-0218 was a double-blinded, randomized, controlled trial that included 1,873 women with stage III or IV disease, all of whom received chemotherapy&#8212;carboplatin (AUC, 6) and paclitaxel (175 mg/m<span class="sup">

36932</span>

3694 for six cycles). Forty percent of the women had suboptimally resected stage III disease, and 26% had stage IV disease. The primary end point of the study was PFS.[<a href="#cit/section_6.50">

369550</a>

3696][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3697Level of evidence B1</a>

3698] Participants were randomly assigned to receive the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

3699<ul id="_863">

3700<li>

3701Chemotherapy plus placebo (cycles 2&#8211;22) (the control group).</li>

3702<li>

3703 Chemotherapy plus bevacizumab (15 mg/kg cycles 2&#8211;6), followed by placebo (cycles 7&#8211;22) (the bevacizumab-initiation group). </li>

3704<li>

3705Chemotherapy plus bevacizumab (15 mg/kg cycles 2&#8211;22) (the bevacizumab-throughout group).</li>

3706</ul>

3707</div>

3708<p id="_864" tabindex="-1">

3709Results from the trial demonstrated the following:</p>

3710<div class="pdq-content-list">

3711<ul id="_865">

3712<li>

3713There was no difference in PFS between the control group and the bevacizumab-initiation group.</li>

3714<li>

3715There was a statistically significant increase in PFS in the bevacizumab-throughout group when compared with the control group (14.1 months vs. 10.3 months), with an HR<sub>

3716 disease progression</sub>

3717 or<sub>

3718 death</sub>

3719 of 0.717 in the bevacizumab-throughout group (95% CI, 0.625&#8211;0.824; <em>

3720P</em>

3721 &lt; .001).</li>

3722<li>

3723Median OS was 39.3 months for the control group, 38.7 months for the bevacizumab-initiation group, and 39.7 months for the bevacizumab-throughout group. </li>

3724<li>

3725Quality of life was not different between the three groups. Hypertension of grade 2 or higher was more common with bevacizumab than with placebo.</li>

3726<li>

3727There were more treatment-related deaths in the bevacizumab-throughout arm (10 of 607, 2.3%) than in the control arm (6 of 601, 1.0%).</li>

3728</ul>

3729</div>

3730</li>

3731<li>

3732ICON7 randomly assigned 1,528 women after initial surgery to chemotherapy&#8212;carboplatin (AUC, 5 or 6) plus paclitaxel (175 mg/m<span class="sup">

37332</span>

3734 for six cycles)&#8212;or to chemotherapy plus bevacizumab (7.5 mg/kg for six cycles), followed by bevacizumab alone for an additional 12 cycles. Nine percent of patients had early-stage, high-grade tumors; 70% had stage IIIC or IV disease; and 26% had more than 1 cm of residual tumor before initiating chemotherapy. PFS was the main outcome measure.[<a href="#cit/section_6.51">

373551</a>

3736][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3737Level of evidence B1</a>

3738]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3739<ol id="_1006" class="lower-alpha">

3740<li>

3741Median PFS was 17.3 months in the control group and 19 months in the bevacizumab group. HR<sub>

3742 disease progression</sub>

3743 or<sub>

3744 death</sub>

3745 in the bevacizumab group was 0.81 (95% CI, 0.70&#8211;0.94; <em>

3746P</em>

3747 = .004).</li>

3748<li>

3749Grade 3 or higher adverse events were more common in the bevacizumab group, with an increase in bleeding, hypertension (grade 2 or higher), thromboembolic events (grade 3 or higher), and gastrointestinal perforations.</li>

3750<li>

3751Quality of life was not different between the two groups.</li>

3752<li>

3753In 2015, the ICON7 authors reported an updated survival analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_6.33">

375433</a>

3755]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3756<ul id="_1008">

3757<li>

3758There was no significant difference with 44.6 months (95% CI, 43.2&#8211;45.9) in patients on standard chemotherapy versus 45.5 months (44.2&#8211;46.7) in patients receiving bevacizumab with the chemotherapy induction, and then completing 1 year of bevacizumab maintenance (log-rank <em>

3759P</em>

3760 = .85). </li>

3761</ul>

3762</div>

3763</li>

3764</ol>

3765</div>

3766</li>

3767</ol>

3768</div>

3769<p id="_1403" tabindex="-1">

3770Supported by these two studies, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) approved bevacizumab in the first-line setting, both during induction and as consolidation therapy. Bevacizumab had first gained approval in the platinum-resistant setting (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00976911">

3771AURELIA</a>

3772 trial [NCT00976911]). </p>

3773</section>

3774<section id="_1123">

3775<h4 id="_1123_toc">

3776Surgery before or after platinum-based chemotherapy and the addition of poly (ADP-ribose) polymerase (PARP) inhibitors to induction and/or consolidation therapy</h4>

3777<p id="_1124" tabindex="-1">

3778PARP is a family of enzymes involved in base-excision repair of DNA single-strand breaks. In patients with homologous recombination deficiency, including patients with germline <em class="gene-name">

3779BRCA1</em>

3780 or <em class="gene-name">

3781BRCA2</em>

3782 (g<em class="gene-name">

3783BRCA</em>

3784) mutations or with nongermline homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;positive tumors, the inhibition of PARP results in the production of double-strand breaks of DNA. Human DNA repair mechanisms largely rely on one intact copy of the gene. Cells with a double-strand break are usually targeted for cell death. This susceptibility of <em class="gene-name">

3785BRCA</em>

3786-deficient or <em class="gene-name">

3787BRCA</em>

3788-mutant cells to PARP inhibition,[<a href="#cit/section_6.52">

378952</a>

3790,<a href="#cit/section_6.53">

379153</a>

3792] has spurred the clinical development of this class of agents. Initially, these agents were tested in women who had been pretreated with chemotherapy. For more information, see the <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_957">

3793Bevacizumab, other targeted drugs, and poly (ADP-ribose) polymerase (PARP) inhibitors with or without chemotherapy</a>

3794 section.</p>

3795<p id="_1125" tabindex="-1">

3796Evidence (surgery before or after chemotherapy and PARP inhibitors):</p>

3797<div class="pdq-content-list">

3798<ol id="_1126">

3799<li>

3800A double-blind phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01844986">

3801SOLO-1</a>

3802) (NCT01844986) compared maintenance olaparib (300 mg tablets bid) with a placebo. Enrolled patients had newly diagnosed, high-grade serous or endometrioid advanced ovarian cancer with mutations of <em class="gene-name">

3803BRCA1</em>

3804, <em class="gene-name">

3805BRCA2</em>

3806, or both, who had a complete or partial clinical response after platinum-based chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.54">

380754</a>

3808] The study of 391 randomly assigned patients ran from September 2013 to March 2015. Of those patients, 260 were assigned to receive olaparib, and 131 patients were assigned to receive a placebo. All but three patients had germline mutations in <em class="gene-name">

3809BRCA1</em>

3810 (n = 191) or <em class="gene-name">

3811BRCA2</em>

3812 (n = 66). The analysis of the primary end point was stopped after 2 years if there was no evidence of disease or was continued until investigator-assessed disease progression. Patients with partial responses at 2 years were permitted to receive the intervention in a blinded manner. Crossover was not specified, but after discontinuation, patients could receive treatments at the discretion of the investigator. The primary end point was PFS, which was defined as from the time of randomization to objective disease progression on imaging (q 12 weeks up to 3 years), or death from any cause. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3813<ol id="_1437" class="lower-alpha">

3814<li>

3815After a median follow-up of 41 months, the risk of disease progression or death was 70% lower with olaparib than with a placebo (Kaplan-Meier estimates of PFS at 3 years, 60% vs. 27%; HR, 0.3; 95% CI, 0.23&#8211;0.41; <em>

3816P</em>

3817 &lt; .001). </li>

3818<li>

3819Grades 3 and 4 adverse events were present in 39% of the patients who received olaparib versus 18% who received a placebo. The most common events with olaparib were fatigue, vomiting, and anemia. Drug discontinuation occurred in 12% of the patients who received olaparib versus 2% who received a placebo.</li>

3820<li>

3821No significant changes in quality of life occurred in either group.[<a href="#cit/section_6.54">

382254</a>

3823][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3824Level of evidence B1</a>

3825]</li>

3826<li>

3827The results of an updated analysis indicated that the risk of disease progression or death was reduced as follows:[<a href="#cit/section_6.55">

382855</a>

3829]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3830<ul id="_1434">

3831<li>

3832By 69% with olaparib (HR, 0.31; 95% CI, 0.21&#8211;0.46) compared with 63% with placebo (HR, 0.37; 95% CI, 0.24&#8211;0.58) in patients undergoing up-front or interval surgery;</li>

3833<li>

3834By 56% with olaparib (HR, 0.44; 95% CI, 0.25&#8211;0.77) compared with 67% with placebo (HR, 0.33; 95% CI, 0.23&#8211;0.46) in patients with residual or no residual disease after surgery; </li>

3835<li>

3836By 66% with olaparib (HR, 0.34; 95% CI, 0.24&#8211;0.47) compared with 69% with placebo (HR, 0.31; 95% CI, 0.18&#8211;0.52) in women with clinical complete response or partial response at baseline; and</li>

3837<li>

3838 By 59% with olaparib (HR, 0.41; 95% CI, 0.30&#8211;0.56) compared with 80% with placebo (HR, 0.20; 95% CI, 0.10&#8211;0.37) in patients with a <em class="gene-name">

3839BRCA1</em>

3840 or <em class="gene-name">

3841BRCA2</em>

3842 mutation.</li>

3843</ul>

3844</div>

3845</li>

3846</ol>

3847</div>

3848</li>

3849<li>

3850A double-blind phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02655016">

3851PRIMA</a>

3852 [NCT02655016]) compared maintenance niraparib (300 mg tablets once daily and later amended to 200 mg in women &lt;77 kg and/or baseline platelet count &lt;150,000/&#181;L) versus placebo in patients with high-grade serous ovarian cancer before the last cycle of platinum-based chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.56">

385356</a>

3854] Homologous recombination deficiency as determined by myChoice (Myriad) was present in 50.9% of patients. In a 2:1 randomization (niraparib, n = 487; placebo, n = 246) from June 2016 to May 2018, patients were assigned for comparison of primary end points of PFS for homologous recombination deficiency (50.9%) and for the overall population. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3855<ol id="_1438" class="lower-alpha">

3856<li>

3857At a median follow-up of 13.8 months, the risk of progression in the homologous recombination deficiency population had an HR of 0.43 (95% CI, 0.31&#8722;0.59; <em>

3858P</em>

3859 &lt; .001) corresponding to a median PFS of 21.9 months versus 10.4 months favoring the drug compared with the placebo. In the overall population selected for this trial, the HR was 0.62, which corresponded to a median PFS of 13.8 months versus 8.2 months (95% CI, 0.50&#8722;0.76; <em>

3860P</em>

3861 &lt; .001).</li>

3862<li>

3863Grade 3 or higher adverse events, none fatal, consisted of anemia in 31% of patients, thrombocytopenia in 28.7% of patients, and neutropenia in 12.8% of patients; 58 of 307 discontinuations of niraparib were caused by adverse events versus 5 of 175 discontinuations of the placebo. </li>

3864</ol>

3865</div>

3866</li>

3867<li>

3868<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02470585">

3869VELIA/GOG-3005</a>

3870 (NCT02470585), a phase III placebo-controlled study, assessed the efficacy of oral veliparib added to first-line induction chemotherapy with carboplatin/paclitaxel and continued as maintenance chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.57">

387157</a>

3872] The study randomly assigned 1,140 patients in a 1:1:1 ratio to receive chemotherapy plus placebo followed by placebo maintenance, chemotherapy plus veliparib followed by placebo maintenance, and chemotherapy plus veliparib induction and maintenance (labeled as &#8216;veliparib throughout&#8217;). Doses of veliparib were 150 mg twice daily during induction, and patients who completed six cycles without progression received single-agent veliparib (or matching placebo) at 300 mg twice daily for 2 weeks (labeled as the transition period), and if no dose-limiting side effects were noted, escalated to 400 mg twice daily for an additional 30 cycles of 3 weeks of oral drug. The study accrued patients from July 2015 to July 2017, and the data was analyzed at a median 28 months duration of follow-up. As in the PRIMA study above, efficacy analyses were performed in three sequential inclusive populations: 1) the <em class="gene-name">

3873BRCA</em>

3874 mutation cohort, 2) the homologous recombination deficiency cohort (that included the preceding cohort), and 3) the intention-to-treat population. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3875<ol id="_1439" class="lower-alpha">

3876<li>

3877At a median follow-up of 28 months, the <em class="gene-name">

3878BRCA</em>

3879-mutation cohort experienced a PFS of 34.7 months with veliparib throughout versus 22.0 months in the chemotherapy-only arm (induction veliparib added without veliparib maintenance was not compared). This corresponded to an HR of 0.44 (95% CI, 0.28&#8722;0.68; <em>

3880P</em>

3881 &lt; .001). </li>

3882<li>

3883For the homologous recombination deficiency population, PFS occurred at a median of 31.9 months for the veliparib throughout arm versus 20.5 months for the chemotherapy-alone arm, with an HR of 0.57 (95% CI, 0.43&#8722;0.76; <em>

3884P</em>

3885 &lt; .001). </li>

3886<li>

3887In the overall population selected, the median PFS was 23.5 months for the veliparib throughout arm versus 17.3 months for the chemotherapy-alone arm, corresponding to an HR of 0.68 (95% CI, 0.56&#8722;0.83; <em>

3888P</em>

3889 &lt; .001).</li>

3890<li>

3891 Veliparib contributed to a higher rate of anemia and thrombocytopenia when combined with chemotherapy, and contributed overall to nausea and fatigue. Adverse events unrelated to progression during the maintenance phase lead to drug discontinuation in 82 patients. Forty of 377 patients going onto maintenance therapy in the veliparib throughout cohort withdrew consent for the trial drug, 22 patients in the chemotherapy-plus-placebo cohort of 371 patients withdrew consent for the trial drug, and 24 patients in the veliparib only as maintenance (not further analyzed in the comparisons) cohort of 383 patients withdrew consent for the trial drug. </li>

3892</ol>

3893</div>

3894</li>

3895<li>

3896<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02477644">

3897PAOLA1</a>

3898 (NCT02477644), a placebo-controlled trial, compared first-line chemotherapy with carboplatin/paclitaxel followed by bevacizumab maintenance for 2 years, to the inclusion of olaparib versus placebo in the maintenance phase.[<a href="#cit/section_6.58">

389958</a>

3900] This study included 537 patients who were assessed for <em class="gene-name">

3901BRCA</em>

3902 mutations (including somatic mutations) and a nonhomologous recombination deficiency cohort. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3903<ol id="_1440" class="lower-alpha">

3904<li>

3905PFS in the 29% of patients with <em class="gene-name">

3906BRCA</em>

3907 mutations was 37.2 months for bevacizumab-plus-olaparib group versus 21.7 months for the bevacizumab-alone maintenance group, which corresponded to an HR of 0.31. </li>

3908<li>

3909For the non-<em class="gene-name">

3910BRCA</em>

3911 population, the HR was 0.71, which corresponded to a median PFS of 18.9 months versus 16.0 months. </li>

3912<li>

3913For the overall population, the HR was 0.59, which corresponded to a PFS of 22.1 months for the bevacizumab-plus-olaparib group versus 16.6 months for the bevacizumab-alone maintenance group.</li>

3914</ol>

3915</div>

3916</li>

3917</ol>

3918</div>

3919</section>

3920<section id="_817">

3921<h4 id="_817_toc">

3922Other consolidation and/or maintenance therapy trials</h4>

3923<p id="_776" tabindex="-1">

3924Phase III trials of consolidation and/or maintenance therapy have been carried out with cytotoxic drugs, small molecules,[<a href="#cit/section_6.59">

392559</a>

3926] vaccines,[<a href="#cit/section_6.60">

392760</a>

3928] and radioimmunoconjugates [<a href="#cit/section_6.61">

392961</a>

3930] with negative results. Extending the duration of paclitaxel has resulted in modest lengthening of PFS in randomized trials,[<a href="#cit/section_6.62">

393162</a>

3932,<a href="#cit/section_6.63">

393363</a>

3934] but was not adopted as a standard treatment after a subsequent trial.</p>

3935<p id="_1461" tabindex="-1">

3936Evidence (other consolidation and/or maintenance therapy):</p>

3937<div class="pdq-content-list">

3938<ol id="_1462">

3939<li>

3940 The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02718417">

3941JAVELIN OVARIAN 100</a>

3942 study (NCT02718417) was the first published randomized trial of a checkpoint inhibitor (avelumab, an anti&#8211;programmed death-ligand 1 [PD-L1] antibody) in patients with previously untreated epithelial ovarian, fallopian tube, or peritoneal cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_6.64">

394364</a>

3944] Between May 2016 and January 2018, 998 patients were randomly assigned to receive either chemotherapy plus avelumab induction followed by avelumab maintenance (n = 331); chemotherapy followed by avelumab maintenance (n = 332); or chemotherapy followed by observation (n = 335).<div class="pdq-content-list">

3945<ul id="_1463">

3946<li>

3947 The study was terminated at interim analysis for futility of reaching the primary end point of improved PFS. </li>

3948<li>

3949More patients in the avelumab arms discontinued study treatment and experienced grade 3 to 5 serious adverse events than patients in the chemotherapy-alone arm.</li>

3950</ul>

3951</div>

3952</li>

3953<li>

3954<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03038100">

3955IMagyn050</a>

3956 (NCT03038100) was a multicenter, placebo-controlled, double-blind, randomized phase III trial of platinum-based chemotherapy and bevacizumab with or without atezolizumab, an anti&#8211;PD-L1 antibody. The study reported negative results in the first-line arms for patients who received atezolizumab.[<a href="#cit/section_6.65">

395765</a>

3958] </li>

3959</ol>

3960</div>

3961</section>

3962<section id="_1474">

3963<h4 id="_1474_toc">

3964Treatment options under clinical evaluation</h4>

3965<p id="_1475" tabindex="-1">

3966Trials are ongoing with antiangiogenic drugs (other than bevacizumab) and with PARP inhibitors. PARP is a family of enzymes involved in base-excision repair of DNA single-strand breaks. In patients with homologous recombination deficiency, including patients with germline <em class="gene-name">

3967BRCA1</em>

3968 or <em class="gene-name">

3969BRCA2</em>

3970 (g<em class="gene-name">

3971BRCA</em>

3972) mutations or with nongermline homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;positive tumors, inhibition of PARP results in production of double-strand breaks of DNA. Human DNA repair mechanisms largely rely on one intact copy of the gene; cells with a double-strand break are usually targeted for cell death. This susceptibility of <em class="gene-name">

3973BRCA</em>

3974-deficient or <em class="gene-name">

3975BRCA</em>

3976-mutant cells to PARP inhibition [<a href="#cit/section_6.52">

397752</a>

3978,<a href="#cit/section_6.53">

397953</a>

3980] has spurred the clinical development of this class of agents. Sensitivity to platinum compounds is a feature of homologous recombination deficiency, and a population of platinum-sensitive patients is expected to be homologous recombination deficiency enriched and most likely to benefit from PARP inhibition.</p>

3981<p id="_1476" tabindex="-1">

3982Information about ongoing clinical trials is available from the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

3983NCI website</a>

3984.</p>

3985</section>

3994General information</a>

3995 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4266

4267 <section id="_82">

4268

4269 <h2>

4270Treatment of Recurrent or Persistent Ovarian Epithelial Cancer, FTC, and PPC</h2>

4271

4272 <div id="_section_82" class="pdq-sections">

4273<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4274<h6>

4275In This Section</h6>

4276<ul>

4277<li>

4278<a href="#_690_toc">

4279Treatment Options for Patients with Recurrent or Persistent Ovarian Epithelial Cancer, FTC, and PPC<ul>

4280<li>

4281<a href="#_903_toc">

4282Platinum-sensitive recurrence</a>

4283</li>

4284<li>

4285<a href="#_993_toc">

4286Platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrence</a>

4287</li>

4288</ul>

4289</a>

4290</li>

4291<li>

4292<a href="#_TrialSearch_82_sid_7_toc">

4293Current Clinical Trials</a>

4294</li>

4295</ul>

4296</nav>

4297<p id="_781" tabindex="-1">

4298Approximately 80% of patients diagnosed with ovarian epithelial cancer, fallopian tube cancer (FTC), and primary peritoneal cancer (PPC) will relapse after first-line platinum-based and taxane-based chemotherapy and may benefit from subsequent therapies. Early detection of persistent disease by second-look laparotomies after completion of first-line treatment is no longer practiced. When the outcomes in institutions practicing such procedures (50% of institutions) were informally compared with the outcomes in institutions not using such procedures, lack of support for second-look laparotomies grew. This was confirmed in the Gynecologic Oncology Group (GOG) GOG-0158 trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

42991</a>

4300] </p>

4301<p id="_951" tabindex="-1">

4302However, the practice of close follow-up of patients completing treatment by measuring cancer antigen 125 (CA-125) levels at intervals of 1 to 3 months was nearly universally adopted. In patients who are in clinical complete remission, increases in CA-125 from their initial treatment represent the most common method to detect disease that will eventually relapse clinically.</p>

4303<p id="_1004" tabindex="-1">

4304Treatment based on abnormal increases in CA-125 in the absence of symptoms or imaging evidence of disease has been addressed in a clinical trial.</p>

4305<p id="_952" tabindex="-1">

4306Evidence (early vs. delayed initiation of treatment):</p>

4307<div class="pdq-content-list">

4308<ol id="_953">

4309<li>

4310A trial by the Medical Research Council (MRC) (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00002895">

4311MRC-OV05</a>

4312) and the European Organisation for Research and Treatment of Cancer examined the consequences of early treatment for an elevated CA-125 level versus treatment delayed until clinical symptoms appeared.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

43132</a>

4314] Patients in clinical complete remission after platinum-based chemotherapy were registered and followed with CA-125 levels and clinical visits only. Upon detection of a twofold elevation over the normal range, patients were randomly assigned to disclosure of the result and early treatment for recurrence versus continued blinding and treatment upon development of signs and symptoms indicative of clinical relapse. The number of randomly assigned patients was to exceed 500 to yield a superior survival outcome at 2 years with early institution of therapy; this required 1,400 registrations, which were accrued between May 1996 and August 2005.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4315<ul id="_954">

4316<li>

4317Among 1,442 patients, 29% continued to show no evidence of relapse; however, in 19% of patients, the CA-125 level was noninformative at clinical relapse, or a doubling occurred concurrently with clinical relapse.</li>

4318<li>

4319Patients had stage III and stage IV disease in 67% of the cases; however, these stages represented 80% of the patients with a twofold or higher increase in CA-125 level who subsequently were randomly assigned.</li>

4320<li>

4321The median survival of all patients registered was 70.8 months.</li>

4322<li>

4323Median survival for patients randomly assigned to early treatment (n = 265) was 25.7 months compared with 27.1 months for patients in the delayed-treatment group (n = 264) (hazard ratio [HR], 0.98; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.8&#8211;1.2). </li>

4324<li>

4325The median delay in instituting second-line chemotherapy was 4.8 months, and the median delay in instituting third-line chemotherapy was 4.6 months. Second-line chemotherapy treatments were comparable among the two groups (mostly platinum- and taxane-based), whereas third-line treatments were less often applied to the delayed-treatment group. </li>

4326<li>

4327The study concluded that there was no benefit in the detection of early presence of disease by CA-125. This finding is consistent with the failure of second-look surgeries to provide improved outcomes after early detection of persistent disease.</li>

4328</ul>

4329</div>

4330</li>

4331</ol>

4332</div>

4333<p id="_1053" tabindex="-1">

4334A quality-of-life assessment accompanying this study found a detrimental effect in the early treatment when it was compared with waiting for the development of signs and symptoms.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

43353</a>

4336] </p>

4337<p id="_783" tabindex="-1">

4338The impact of these findings on CA-125 surveillance patterns over a decade in five U.S. Cancer Centers was disappointingly low.[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

43394</a>

4340,<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

43415</a>

4342] Monitoring CA-125 levels in follow-up was used to separate platinum-sensitive from platinum-resistant recurrences and plays a role in identifying appropriate candidates for secondary cytoreduction, although this strategy awaits confirmation with a randomized trial.</p>

4343<section id="_690">

4344<h3 id="_690_toc">

4345Treatment Options for Patients with Recurrent or Persistent Ovarian Epithelial Cancer, FTC, and PPC</h3>

4346<p id="_870" tabindex="-1">

4347Drug treatment options for patients with recurrent disease are subdivided as follows:</p>

4348<div class="pdq-content-list">

4349<ol id="_784">

4350<li>

4351<a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_903">

4352Platinum-sensitive recurrence</a>

4353: For patients whose disease recurs more than 6 months after cessation of the induction, re-treatment with a platinum or platinum-containing combination, such as carboplatin, should be considered (see <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4354Table 8</a>

4355).

4356</li>

4357<li>

4358<a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_993">

4359 Platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrence</a>

4360: For patients who progress before cessation of induction therapy (platinum refractory) or within 6 months after cessation of induction therapy (platinum resistant), platinum therapy is generally not useful as part of the treatment plan. Clinical trials should be considered.</li>

4361</ol>

4362</div>

4363<p id="_785" tabindex="-1">

4364Other agents that have shown activity in phase II trials are listed in <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_343">

4365Table 10</a>

4366 and may also be used alone or in combination with other drugs, but such treatments are best done in prospective trials.</p>

4367<p id="_999" tabindex="-1">

4368Cytoreduction may be used;[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

43694</a>

4370] this intervention has been studied in the setting of randomized clinical trials (e.g., <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00565851">

4371GOG-0213</a>

4372 [NCT00565851], <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01166737">

4373DESKTOP III</a>

4374 [NCT01166737], and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01611766">

4375SOC 1</a>

4376 [NCT01611766]). The SOC 1 trial was published with immature survival data.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

43776</a>

4378] Eligibility criteria differed between each of the trials. Only 67% of patients achieved complete gross resections in the GOG-0213 trial,[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

43797</a>

4380] compared with 77% of patients in the SOC 1 trial and 75% of patients in the DESKTOP III trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

43818</a>

4382] The Dutch SOCcer trial was closed prematurely in 2015 because only 27 of 230 planned patients (12%) were accrued in 5 years.[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

43839</a>

4384,<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

438510</a>

4386] In order for the GOG trial to study the role of surgery, the target enrollment was 485 patients which took almost 10 years to achieve. </p>

4387<p id="_944" tabindex="-1">

4388The role of radiation therapy in patients with recurrent ovarian cancer has not been defined.</p>

4389<section id="_903">

4390<h4 id="_903_toc">

4391Platinum-sensitive recurrence</h4>

4392<section id="_989">

4393<h5 id="_989_toc">

4394Platinum-containing chemotherapy regimens</h5>

4395<p id="_955" tabindex="-1">

4396<a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4397Table 8</a>

4398 shows the chemotherapy regimens used in first relapse for the treatment of platinum-sensitive recurrent ovarian cancer.</p>

4399<table id="_789" class="table-default expandable-container">

4620<p id="_871" tabindex="-1">

4621On the basis of improved survival with etoposide or fluorouracil, carboplatin was approved in 1987 for the treatment of patients with ovarian cancer whose disease recurred after treatment with cisplatin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.18">

462218</a>

4623] In a randomized phase II trial of paclitaxel, a currently used second-line drug, the cisplatin-containing combination of

4624cisplatin plus doxorubicin plus cyclophosphamide, yielded a superior survival outcome.[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

462515</a>

4626] This study and subsequent studies (see <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4627Table 8</a>

4628) have reinforced the use of carboplatin as the treatment core for patients with platinum-sensitive recurrences. Cisplatin is occasionally used, particularly in combination with other drugs, because of its lesser myelosuppression, but this advantage over carboplatin is counterbalanced by greater patient intolerance.</p>

4629<p id="_872" tabindex="-1">

4630Oxaliplatin, initially introduced with the hope that it would overcome platinum resistance, has activity mostly in platinum-sensitive patients [<a href="#cit/section_7.19">

463119</a>

4632] but has not been compared with carboplatin alone or in combinations.</p>

4633<p id="_873" tabindex="-1">

4634With all platinum agents, outcome is generally better the longer the initial interval without recurrence from the initial platinum-containing regimens.[<a href="#cit/section_7.20">

463520</a>

4636] Therefore, on occasion, patients with platinum-sensitive recurrences relapsing within 1 year have been included in trials of nonplatinum drugs. In one such trial, comparing the pegylated liposomal doxorubicin to topotecan, the subset of patients who were platinum sensitive had better outcomes with either drug (and in particular with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin) relative to the platinum-resistant cohort.[<a href="#cit/section_7.21">

463721</a>

4638]</p>

4639<p id="_874" tabindex="-1">

4640Several randomized trials have addressed whether the use of a platinum in combination with other chemotherapy agents is superior to single agents (see <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4641Table 8</a>

4642). </p>

4643<p id="_875" tabindex="-1">

4644Evidence (platinum in combination with other chemotherapy agents):</p>

4645<div class="pdq-content-list">

4646<ol id="_1000">

4647<li>

4648In an analysis of data examining jointly the results of trials performed by the MRC/Arbeitsgemeinschaft Gynaekologische Onkologie (MRC/AGO) and the International Collaborative Ovarian Neoplasm (ICON) investigators (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00002894">

4649ICON4</a>

4650), the following results were observed:[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

46515</a>

4652,<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

465314</a>

4654][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4655Level of evidence A1</a>

4656]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4657<ul id="_877">

4658<li>

4659A platinum-plus-paclitaxel combination yielded superior response rates, progression-free survival (PFS), and overall survival (OS), compared with carboplatin as a single agent or other platinum-containing combinations as controls.</li>

4660<li>

4661Platinum plus paclitaxel was compared with several control regimens, although 71% used carboplatin as a single agent in the control, and 80% used carboplatin plus paclitaxel. Prolonged PFS (HR, 0.76; 95% CI, 0.66&#8211;0.89; <em>

4662P</em>

4663 = .004) and OS (HR, 0.82; 95% CI, 0.69&#8211;0.97; <em>

4664P</em>

4665 = .023) were improved in the platinum-plus-paclitaxel arm.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

466614</a>

4667]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

46685</a>

4669][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4670Level of evidence A1</a>

4671]</li>

4672<li>

4673The AGO had previously compared the combination of epirubicin plus carboplatin with carboplatin alone and had not found significant differences in outcome.</li>

4674<li>

4675A meta-analysis of five trials (three of which are in <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4676Table 8</a>

4677), with four reviewing independent patient data, supports the use of platinum agents in combination with other active agents rather than carboplatin alone for patients with platinum-sensitive recurrent ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.22">

467822</a>

4679]</li>

4680</ul>

4681</div>

4682</li>

4683<li>

4684Another trial by European and Canadian groups compared gemcitabine plus carboplatin with carboplatin.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4685<ul id="_878">

4686<li>

4687The PFS of 8.6 months with the combination was significantly superior to 5.8 months for the carboplatin alone (HR, 0.72; 95% CI, 0.58&#8211;0.90; <em>

4688P</em>

4689 = .003).[<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

469012</a>

4691][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4692Level of evidence B1</a>

4693]</li>

4694<li>

4695The study was not powered to detect significant differences in OS, and the median survival for both arms was 18 months (HR, 0.96; CI, 0.75&#8211;1.23; <em>

4696P</em>

4697 = .73).</li>

4698</ul>

4699</div>

4700</li>

4701<li>

4702In a phase III trial, carboplatin plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin was compared with carboplatin plus paclitaxel in patients with platinum-sensitive recurrence (&gt;6 months). The primary end point was PFS. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4703<ul id="_991">

4704<li>

4705The median PFS for the carboplatin-plus-pegylated-liposomal-doxorubicin arm was 11.3 months versus 9.4 months for the carboplatin-plus-paclitaxel arm (HR, 0.823; 95% CI, 0.72&#8211;0.94; <em>

4706P</em>

4707 = .005).[<a href="#cit/section_7.23">

470823</a>

4709][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4710Level of evidence B1</a>

4711]</li>

4712<li>

4713Long-term follow-up revealed no difference in OS rates between the two arms (30.7 months for carboplatin plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin vs. 33.0 months for carboplatin plus paclitaxel).[<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

471413</a>

4715]</li>

4716<li>

4717The carboplatin-plus-paclitaxel arm was associated with increased severe neutropenia, alopecia, neuropathy, and allergic reaction. The carboplatin-plus-pegylated-liposomal-doxorubicin arm was associated with increased severe thrombocytopenia, nausea, and hand-foot syndrome.</li>

4718</ul>

4719</div>

4720<p id="_992" tabindex="-1">

4721Given its toxicity profile and noninferiority to the standard regimen, carboplatin plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin is an important option for patients with platinum-sensitive recurrence.</p>

4722</li>

4723</ol>

4724</div>

4725<p id="_904" tabindex="-1">

4726Carboplatin plus paclitaxel has been considered the standard regimen for platinum-sensitive recurrence in the absence of residual neurological toxic effects. The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00565851">

4727GOG-0213</a>

4728 trial is comparing this regimen with the experimental arm that adds bevacizumab to carboplatin plus paclitaxel.</p>

4729</section>

4730<section id="_957">

4731<h5 id="_957_toc">

4732Bevacizumab, other targeted drugs, and poly (ADP-ribose) polymerase (PARP) inhibitors with or without chemotherapy</h5>

4733<p id="_958" tabindex="-1">

4734Evidence (bevacizumab with gemcitabine/carboplatin):</p>

4735<div class="pdq-content-list">

4736<ol id="_959">

4737<li>

4738The Ovarian Cancer Study Comparing Efficacy and Safety of Chemotherapy and Anti-Angiogenic Therapy in Platinum-Sensitive Recurrent Diseases (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00434642">

4739OCEANS</a>

4740 [NCT00434642]) assessed the role of bevacizumab in the treatment of platinum-sensitive recurrence (see <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4741Table 8</a>

4742 for other trials in this setting). In this double-blind, placebo-controlled, phase III trial of chemotherapy (gemcitabine plus carboplatin) with or without bevacizumab for recurrent ovarian epithelial cancer, FTC, or PPC, 242 patients were randomly assigned to each arm. In contrast to the first-line studies, treatment was allowed to continue beyond six cycles to ten cycles in responding patients, but there was no maintenance therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

474324</a>

4744]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4745<ul id="_961">

4746<li>

4747A subsequent analysis will appear when additional survival data become mature; however, at the time of publication, differences in median OS were not apparent, and crossover from a placebo to bevacizumab had occurred in 31% of the patients. </li>

4748<li>

4749Median PFS for patients receiving bevacizumab was 12.4 months versus 8.4 months for those receiving a placebo.</li>

4750<li>

4751The HR for the effect of bevacizumab on disease progression in patients assigned to the bevacizumab arm compared with placebo was 0.484 (95% CI, 0.388&#8211;0.605; <em>

4752P</em>

4753 &lt; .0001).</li>

4754<li>

4755Objective responses to chemotherapy were increased when combined with bevacizumab (78.5% vs. 57.4%; <em>

4756P</em>

4757 &lt; .0001).</li>

4758<li>

4759Bevacizumab-associated toxicities such as hypertension and proteinuria were more prominent than in the first-line trials, but feared safety issues such as gastrointestinal perforations did not occur during the study.</li>

4760<li>

4761Discontinuing treatment because of adverse events was more common with bevacizumab (n = 55 vs. n = 12 for placebo), but fewer patients discontinued treatment because of disease progression (n = 104 for bevacizumab vs. n = 160 for placebo).</li>

4762</ul>

4763</div>

4764</li>

4765</ol>

4766</div>

4767<p id="_1036" tabindex="-1">

4768Evidence (bevacizumab added to carboplatin or carboplatin doublets): </p>

4769<div class="pdq-content-list">

4770<ol id="_1037">

4771<li>

4772NRG Oncology Group, or National Clinical Trials Network group, a combined research effort of the National Surgical Adjuvant Breast and Bowel Project, the Radiation Therapy Oncology Group, and the GOG (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00565851">

4773GOG-0213</a>

4774 [NCT00565851]) assessed both the role of surgical debulking and the addition of bevacizumab induction and maintenance in women with platinum-sensitive recurrences of ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

47757</a>

4776][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4777Level of evidence A1</a>

4778] The nonsurgical portion of GOG-0213 had 81% power for a true HR of 0.75; it enrolled 674 women from December 2007 to August 2011, and the published analysis took place after a median follow-up exceeding 4 years. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4779<ul id="_1038">

4780<li>

4781OS was not significantly different: 37.3 months (95% CI, 32.6&#8211;39.7) versus 42.2 months (95% CI, 37.7&#8211;46.2).</li>

4782<li>

4783The secondary end point of median PFS was significantly in favor of the addition of bevacizumab: 10.4 months (95% CI, 9.7&#8211;11) for chemotherapy alone versus 13.8 months (95% CI, 13.0&#8211;14.7). </li>

4784<li>

4785Bevacizumab (15 mg/kg q 3 weeks) with chemotherapy and its use in maintenance led to an excess of grade 3 and 4 adverse events (8% for chemotherapy alone vs. 30%), any bleeding (12% vs. 42%), and any hypertension (3% vs. 41%). </li>

4786</ul>

4787</div>

4788</li>

4789<li>

4790In an open-label, randomized, phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01802749">

4791MITO16b/MANGO-OV2/ENGOT-ov17</a>

4792 [NCT01802749]), investigators enrolled 406 patients at first recurrence or progression at least 6 months after receiving first-line platinum-based treatment, including bevacizumab during induction or maintenance.[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

479317</a>

4794] The trial compared carboplatin doublets with or without bevacizumab as standard treatment for patients with platinum-sensitive recurrence. Dosing schedules varied with each doublet and all bevacizumab was given at a dose rate of 5 mg/kg/week. Twenty-one patients received carboplatin/paclitaxel and 22 patients received carboplatin/paclitaxel plus bevacizumab; 99 patients received cisplatin/gemcitabine and 98 patients received cisplatin/gemcitabine plus bevacizumab; and 83 patients received pegylated liposomal doxorubicin and 83 patients received pegylated liposomal doxorubicin plus bevacizumab. Patients were accrued in the study between December 2013 and November 2016. The primary end point was investigator-assessed PFS, seeking to reduce the HR for recurrence to 0.67 (90% power and two-tailed test at alpha = .05). Secondary end points were OS (from time of randomization to death from any cause) and objective response rates according to Response Evaluation Criteria in Solid Tumors (RECIST). <div class="pdq-content-list">

4795<ul id="_1452">

4796<li>

4797Median PFS was 8.8 months (95% CI, 8.4&#8211;9.3) for patients in the standard chemotherapy arm versus 11.8 months (HR, 0.51; 95% CI, 10.8&#8211;12.9) for patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm.[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

479817</a>

4799][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4800Level of evidence B1</a>

4801]</li>

4802<li>

4803 OS was not different between the two groups: median OS was 27.1 months for patients in the standard arm versus 26.7 months for patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm.</li>

4804<li>

4805 Objective response rate analysis determined that 71 of 143 patients in the standard arm and 90 of 130 patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm had either complete or partial responses.</li>

4806<li>

4807 The safety population included 200 patients in the standard arm and 201 patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm. Numerous serious adverse events were recorded in both arms: 61 events for 41 patients in the standard arm and 76 events for 52 patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm.</li>

4808<li>

4809 Hypertension was a major adverse event. In the standard arm, 93% of patients experienced hypertension: 166 patients experienced grade 1 or 2 hypertension and 20 patients experienced grade 3 hypertension. In the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm, 98% of patients experienced hypertension: 139 patients experienced grade 1 or 2 hypertension and 58 patients experienced grade 3 hypertension.</li>

4810<li>

4811 Proteinuria and epistaxis were also prominent grade 1 or 2 adverse events for patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm.</li>

4812</ul>

4813</div>

4814<p id="_1453" tabindex="-1">

4815The study demonstrated that the addition of bevacizumab improved PFS but did not result in any OS benefit and was associated with increased toxicity. This study preceded incorporation of PARP inhibitors in phase III trials for patients with platinum-sensitive recurrence. In a subset analysis of patients with <em class="gene-name">

4816BRCA</em>

4817 mutations in this study, only 23 patients in the standard arm and 30 patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm had documented deleterious mutations. These details underscore the evolution of targeted treatment that has occurred during and after this study. </p>

4818</li>

4819</ol>

4820</div>

4821<p id="_1411" tabindex="-1">

4822

4823Evidence (bevacizumab plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin/carboplatin vs. bevacizumab plus gemcitabine/carboplatin):</p>

4824<p id="_1412" tabindex="-1">

4825 For the results of clinical trials that used gemcitabine/carboplatin, see <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_789">

4826Table 8</a>

4827.[<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

482816</a>

4829,<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

483024</a>

4831] Adverse events differed among the two comparators but serious adverse events were 10% with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin/carboplatin and 9% with gemcitabine/carboplatin. Specifically, hypertensive crisis, presumably related to bevacizumab, occurred in five patients after receiving pegylated liposomal doxorubicin/carboplatin and in three patients after receiving gemcitabine/carboplatin.

4832</p>

4833<p id="_1054" tabindex="-1">

4834Evidence (PARP inhibitors with or without antiangiogenic agents): </p>

4835<p id="_1055" tabindex="-1">

4836PARP is a family of enzymes involved in base-excision repair of DNA single-strand breaks. In patients with homologous recombination deficiency, including patients with germline <em class="gene-name">

4837BRCA1</em>

4838 or <em class="gene-name">

4839BRCA2</em>

4840 (g<em class="gene-name">

4841BRCA</em>

4842) mutations or with nongermline homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;positive tumors, inhibition of PARP results in production of double-strand breaks of DNA. Human DNA repair mechanisms largely rely on one intact copy of the gene; cells with a double-strand break are usually targeted for cell death. This susceptibility of <em class="gene-name">

4843BRCA</em>

4844-deficient or <em class="gene-name">

4845BRCA</em>

4846-mutant cells to PARP inhibition [<a href="#cit/section_7.25">

484725</a>

4848,<a href="#cit/section_7.26">

484926</a>

4850] has spurred the clinical development of this class of agents. Sensitivity to platinum compounds is a feature of homologous recombination deficiency, and a population of platinum-sensitive patients is expected to be homologous recombination deficiency-enriched and most likely to benefit from PARP inhibition. Clinical studies with olaparib have been ongoing since 2005 when a phase I study enrolled women with ovarian cancer who were known <em class="gene-name">

4851BRCA</em>

4852 mutation carriers. Because of objective responses in this initial trial, olaparib, and subsequently rucaparib and niraparib, have been studied after several lines of treatment for recurrence; these studies lead to an initial approval for olaparib, and then rucaparib and niraparib, as listed in <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_1413">

4853Table 9</a>

4854.</p>

4855<table id="_1413" class="table-default expandable-container">

4856<caption>

4857Table 9. Indications for PARP Inhibitors in Ovarian Cancer</caption>

4858<colgroup>

4859<col width="14.12%">

4860<col width="14.12%">

4861<col width="17.36%">

4862<col width="11.57%">

4863<col width="14.12%">

4864<col width="14.12%">

4865<col width="14.58%">

4866</colgroup>
