5009</table>

5010<div class="pdq-content-list">

5011<ol id="_1056">

5012<li>

5013In a randomized, double blind, placebo-controlled phase II trial of olaparib maintenance therapy, eligible patients had platinum-sensitive, high-grade serous ovarian cancer. Patients were randomly assigned to receive olaparib (400 mg bid) or placebo. Having a g<em class="gene-name">

5014BRCA1</em>

5015 or g<em class="gene-name">

5016BRCA2</em>

5017 mutation was not required for eligibility; however, 23% of patients in the experimental group and 22% of patients in the placebo group had a known <em class="gene-name">

5018BRCA1</em>

5019 or <em class="gene-name">

5020BRCA2</em>

5021 mutation. The primary end point was PFS.[<a href="#cit/section_7.27">

502227</a>

5023][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5024Level of evidence B1</a>

5025] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5026<ul id="_1057">

5027<li>

5028Median PFS was 8.4 months for patients in the olaparib arm versus 4.8 months for patients in the placebo arm (HR, 0.35; 95% CI, 0.25&#8211;0.49; <em>

5029P</em>

5030 &lt; .001).</li>

5031<li>

5032OS was not different between the two groups, as noted in an updated report.[<a href="#cit/section_7.28">

503328</a>

5034]</li>

5035<li>

5036The more common adverse events in the olaparib group were nausea, fatigue, vomiting, and anemia.</li>

5037</ul>

5038</div>

5039</li>

5040<li>

5041Olaparib tablets (as opposed to the previous capsule formulation) underwent evaluation in <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01874353">

5042SOLO2</a>

5043 (NCT01874353), a double-blind, randomized, placebo-controlled phase III trial in patients with high-grade serous or endometrioid cancer, PPC, or FTC. Patients had platinum-sensitive relapses and were preselected for <em class="gene-name">

5044BRCA1</em>

5045/<em class="gene-name">

5046BRCA2</em>

5047 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_7.29">

504829</a>

5049][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5050Level of evidence B1</a>

5051] Stratification for response (complete vs. partial) to previous platinum and platinum-free intervals (&gt;6&#8211;12 vs. &gt;12 months) and 2:1 random allocation to olaparib in two 150-mg twice-daily or matching placebo tablets took place. Of 295 eligible patients enrolled, 196 were assigned to olaparib, and 99 were assigned to a placebo. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5052<ul id="_1069">

5053<li>

5054The primary end point was PFS and significantly favored olaparib (19.1 months [95% CI, 16.3&#8211;25.7]) more than placebo (5.5 months [range, 5.2&#8211;5.8 months]; HR, 0.30 [95% CI, 0.22&#8211;0.41]; <em>

5055P</em>

5056 &lt; .0001). </li>

5057<li>

5058Serious adverse events were experienced by 18% of patients who received olaparib and by 8% who received placebo.

5059The adverse events consisted mostly of anemia, abdominal pain, and intestinal obstruction.</li>

5060<li>

5061In this trial, a comprehensive assessment of health-related quality-of-life measurements was carried out in patients who received olaparib compared with patients who received placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_7.30">

506230</a>

5063] The Trial Outcome Index score was used in a prespecified analysis of changes, showing that several measurements were met. In addition, time without significant symptoms of toxicity and quality-adjusted PFS were longer in patients who were treated with olaparib. These assessments supplement other measurements such as time to first treatment and time to subsequent therapy or death that have been sought to supplement PFS as a primary end point for drug approval.</li>

5064</ul>

5065</div>

5066

5067</li>

5068<li>

5069The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00628251">

5070SOLO3</a>

5071 trial [NCT00628251], a phase III study that employed 2:1 randomization, compared olaparib tablets with physicians' choice of nonplatinum chemotherapy (pegylated liposomal doxorubicin, weekly paclitaxel, gemcitabine, or topotecan) for the treatment of recurrent platinum-sensitive ovarian cancer and g<em class="gene-name">

5072BRCA1</em>

5073/<em class="gene-name">

5074BRCA2</em>

5075 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_7.31">

507631</a>

5077] A previous randomized phase II study of dose levels of olaparib capsules at either 200 or 400 mg twice daily versus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin had failed to show an advantage over chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.32">

507832</a>

5079] In SOLO3, 178 patients were allocated to receive olaparib and 88 patients received physicians&#8217; choice chemotherapy. The primary end point was overall response rate.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5080<ul id="_1410">

5081<li>

5082Of 151 patients assessed, 109 had objective responses to olaparib (14 complete responses), whereas of 72 patients assessed, 37 had objective responses to chemotherapy (2 complete responses). </li>

5083<li>

5084 At final analysis, there was no significant difference in OS. The median OS was 34.9 months for patients who received olaparib and 32.9 months for patients who received chemotherapy (HR, 1.07; <em>

5085P</em>

5086 = .71).[<a href="#cit/section_7.33">

508733</a>

5088] </li>

5089<li>

5090A subgroup analysis of patients treated with at least three lines of chemotherapy showed a survival detriment. Among these patients, the median OS was 29.9 months in the olaparib group and 39.4 months in the chemotherapy group (HR, 1.33; 95% CI, 0.84&#8211;2.18). </li>

5091<li>

5092Adverse events were consistent with established safety profiles of olaparib and the chemotherapy comparators, but in this pretreated population, four patients assigned to receive olaparib and three patients assigned to receive chemotherapy developed acute myeloid leukemia (AML)/myelodysplasia; new primary malignancies also occurred in three patients assigned to receive olaparib.[<a href="#cit/section_7.31">

509331</a>

5094][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5095Level of evidence B1</a>

5096] </li>

5097<li>

5098 On August 26, 2022, AstraZeneca withdrew the indication for olaparib monotherapy for the treatment of patients with deleterious germline <em class="gene-name">

5099BRCA</em>

5100-mutated ovarian cancer who have received at least three previous lines of chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.34">

510134</a>

5102] </li>

5103</ul>

5104</div>

5105</li>

5106<li>

5107Rucaparib underwent phase II evaluation in <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01891344">

5108ARIEL2</a>

5109 (NCT01891344), an open-label study enrolling 206 patients, 204 of whom were actually receiving the drug (192 were actually in classifiable subgroups) and had high-grade platinum-sensitive recurrences between October 2013 and November 2014.[<a href="#cit/section_7.35">

511035</a>

5111][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5112Level of evidence C2</a>

5113] The following three predefined homologous recombination deficiency subgroups on the basis of tumor mutational analysis were studied:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5114<ul id="_1058">

5115<li>

5116<em class="gene-name">

5117BRCA</em>

5118 mutant (deleterious genetic or somatic) (n = 40).</li>

5119<li>

5120 <em class="gene-name">

5121BRCA</em>

5122 wild type and high loss of heterozygosity (LOH) quantified by next-generation sequencing analysis (LOH high) (n = 82). </li>

5123<li>

5124<em class="gene-name">

5125 BRCA</em>

5126 wild type and low LOH (LOH low) (n = 70).</li>

5127</ul>

5128</div>

5129 The drug was given orally at 600 mg twice daily, and patients were treated until disease progression or other reasons for discontinuation. Median duration of treatment for the 204 patients was 5.7 months. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5130<ul id="_1059">

5131<li>

5132Median PFS after the start of rucaparib treatment for patients with deleterious <em class="gene-name">

5133BRCA</em>

5134 mutations was 12.8 months (95% CI, 9.0&#8211;14.7); for those with LOH, high was 5.7 months (range, 5.3&#8211;7.6 months), and low was 5.2 months (range, 3.6&#8211;5.5 months). </li>

5135<li>

5136The study also showed that mutation and methylation status of <em class="gene-name">

5137BRCA</em>

5138 and other homologous recombination-related genes, such as <em class="gene-name">

5139RAD51C</em>

5140, can be associated with high genomic LOH in <em class="gene-name">

5141BRCA</em>

5142 wild-type tumors, conferring higher rates of response to rucaparib than are seen in patients with low genomic LOH.</li>

5143</ul>

5144</div>

5145 </li>

5146<li>

5147Rucaparib was later assessed as maintenance therapy after response to platinum therapy in a randomized double-blind, placebo-controlled phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01968213">

5148ARIEL3</a>

5149 [NCT01968213]).[<a href="#cit/section_7.36">

515036</a>

5151] To be eligible, patients had high-grade carcinomas that were previously treated with at least two platinum-containing regimens and had achieved complete or partial responses to the last platinum-containing regimen. In a 2:1 treatment allocation, from April 2014 to July 2016, 375 patients received rucaparib, and 189 patients received placebo. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5152<ol id="_1435" class="lower-alpha">

5153<li>

5154PFS, as determined by the investigator, was the primary end point using a step-down procedure for the following three determined, nested treatment cohorts:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5155<ul id="_1436">

5156<li>

5157Patients known to have deleterious germline or somatic <em class="gene-name">

5158BRCA</em>

5159 mutations: PFS of 16.6 months in the

5160rucaparib group (95% CI, 13.4&#8211;22.9) versus 5.4 months in the

5161placebo group (95% CI, 3.4&#8211;6.7; HR, 0.23; 95% CI, 0.16&#8211;0.34; <em>

5162P</em>

5163 &lt; .0001). </li>

5164<li>

5165Patients with homologous recombination deficiencies: PFS of 13.6 months

5166in the rucaparib group (95% CI, 10.9&#8211;16.2) versus 5.4 months in the placebo group (95% CI, 5.1&#8211;5.6; HR, 0.32; 95% CI, 0.24&#8211;0.42;

5167<em>

5168P</em>

5169 &lt; .00011). </li>

5170<li>

5171The intention-to-treat population: PFS of 10.8 months in the rucaparib group (95% CI, 8.3&#8211;11.4) versus 5.4 months in the placebo group (95% CI, 5.3&#8211;5.5; HR, 0.24&#8211;0.42; <em>

5172P </em>

5173&lt; .0001.</li>

5174</ul>

5175</div>

5176</li>

5177<li>

5178Treatment-emergent adverse events of grade 3 or higher in the rucaparib group versus the placebo group consisted primarily of anemia (19% vs. 1%) and increased alanine aminotransferase or aspartate aminotransferase (10% vs. 0%). </li>

5179<li>

5180In an updated outcomes, intention-to-treat, and safety analysis for all cohorts, at a median follow-up of 28 months, rucaparib had significant persistent advantages in PFS compared with placebo (14.3 months vs. 8.8 months [HR, 0.43; 95% CI, 0,35&#8722;0.53]).[<a href="#cit/section_7.37">

518137</a>

5182][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5183Level of evidence B1</a>

5184] </li>

5185<li>

5186Time to first subsequent therapy, time to progression on subsequent therapy, and time to start a second subsequent treatment were also significantly in favor of rucaparib. </li>

5187<li>

5188Three occurrences of AML/myelodysplasia treatment-related events had been previously reported, and treatment-emergent serious adverse events were recorded in 22% of patients who received rucaparib versus 11% of patients who received placebo. </li>

5189<li>

5190Anemia was the most common toxicity attributed to rucaparib (in 22% of patients). </li>

5191<li>

5192In an analysis from this trial of quality-adjusted PFS and quality-adjusted time without symptoms or toxicity, both determinations confirmed that rucaparib was beneficial compared with placebo in all predefined cohorts.[<a href="#cit/section_7.38">

519338</a>

5194] </li>

5195</ol>

5196</div>

5197</li>

5198<li>

5199 The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02855944">

5200ARIEL4</a>

5201 trial (NCT02855944) evaluated rucaparib versus chemotherapy in patients with <em class="gene-name">

5202BRCA</em>

5203-mutated high-grade ovarian epithelial cancer who had been treated with at least two previous lines of chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.39">

520439</a>

5205]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5206<ul id="_1493">

5207<li>

5208 In the intent-to-treat population, the median OS was 19.4 months in the rucaparib group and 25.4 months in the chemotherapy group (HR, 1.31; 95% CI, 1.00&#8211;1.73; <em>

5209P</em>

5210 = .0507). </li>

5211<li>

5212 On June 10, 2022, Clovis Oncology withdrew the indication for rucaparib monotherapy for the treatment of patients with <em class="gene-name">

5213BRCA</em>

5214-mutated cancer who had been treated with at least two previous lines of chemotherapy.</li>

5215</ul>

5216</div>

5217</li>

5218<li>

5219<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02354586">

5220QUADRA</a>

5221 (NCT02354586) was a multicenter, open-label, single-arm phase II trial from 2015 to 2017 that studied niraparib as late-line treatment for patients with ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

522240</a>

5223] It enrolled 463 women who had received a median of four (range, 3&#8722;5) previous regimens (151 patients were platinum resistant and 161 patients were platinum refractory). <div class="pdq-content-list">

5224<ul id="_1395">

5225<li>

5226In the primary efficacy measurable population, 13 of 47 patients responded according to RECIST.[<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

522740</a>

5228][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5229Level of evidence C2</a>

5230] </li>

5231<li>

5232Homologous recombination deficiency was a predictor of response.</li>

5233<li>

5234 Because the makers of olaparib and rucaparib found decreased survival in patients who had received previous chemotherapy when a PARP inhibitor was used as monotherapy, on September 14, 2022, GSK withdrew the indication for niraparib as monotherapy for fourth-line treatment in patients with ovarian epithelial tumors associated with homologous recombination deficiency.[<a href="#cit/section_7.41">

523541</a>

5236]</li>

5237</ul>

5238</div>

5239</li>

5240<li>

5241 Niraparib was evaluated further in a double-blind, placebo-controlled phase III trial of 533 patients with platinum-sensitive, predominantly high-grade serous ovarian cancer, who were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to maintenance with oral niraparib or placebo and followed for the primary end point of PFS.[<a href="#cit/section_7.42">

524242</a>

5243] Patients were categorized according to the presence or absence of g<em class="gene-name">

5244BRCA</em>

5245 or non-<em class="gene-name">

5246BRCA</em>

5247 homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;positive ovarian cancer or non-<em class="gene-name">

5248BRCA</em>

5249 homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;negative ovarian cancer, based on <em class="gene-name">

5250BRCA</em>

5251 <em>

5252Analysis</em>

5253 testing (Myriad Genetics) from tumor and blood samples. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5254<ol id="_1061" class="lower-alpha">

5255<li>

5256Patients who received niraparib had significantly longer median PFS duration compared with a placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_7.42">

525742</a>

5258][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5259Level of evidence B1</a>

5260] Comparisons across categories ranged from HR, 0.27 for g<em class="gene-name">

5261BRCA</em>

5262 cancer (21.0 months vs. 5.5 months), HR, 0.38 for non-<em class="gene-name">

5263BRCA</em>

5264 cancer, homologous recombination deficiency-positive cancer (12.9 months vs. 3.8 months), and HR, 0.45 for non-<em class="gene-name">

5265BRCA</em>

5266, homologous recombination deficiency-negative cancer (9.3 months vs. 3.9 months). </li>

5267<li>

5268Deaths during the study occurred in 16.1% of patients who received niraparib and 19.3% of patients on placebo.</li>

5269<li>

5270One-third to nearly one-half of the patients had received at least three previous lines of therapy that included the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5271<ul id="_1062">

5272<li>

5273Grade 3 or 4 adverse events that were managed with dose modifications while patients received niraparib included thrombocytopenia (in 33.8% of patients), anemia (in 25.3%), and neutropenia (in 19.6%).</li>

5274<li>

5275Other excess severe toxicities in patients who received niraparib occurred at starting doses of 300 mg once daily and included fatigue (in 30 patients vs. 1 patient on the placebo), hypertension (in 30 patients vs. 4 on the placebo), nausea (in 11 patients vs. 2 on the placebo), and vomiting (in 7 patients vs. 1 on the placebo). </li>

5276<li>

5277A subsequent analysis of the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01847274">

5278ENGOT-OV16/NOVA</a>

5279 trial (NCT01847274) updates PFS after maintenance niraparib or placebo according to the best response (partial response [PR] or complete response [CR]) from the last platinum-based chemotherapy in patients with g<em class="gene-name">

5280BRCA</em>

5281 mutations and in non-g<em class="gene-name">

5282BRCA</em>

5283 mutation cohorts.[<a href="#cit/section_7.43">

528443</a>

5285] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5286<ul id="_1396">

5287<li>

5288The HR was significant for niraparib versus placebo, and was seen in both groups. </li>

5289<li>

5290No meaningful differences in patient-reported outcomes were observed.</li>

5291</ul>

5292</div>

5293</li>

5294</ul>

5295</div>

5296</li>

5297<li>

5298A phase III, randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled study of niraparib maintenance in patients with homologous recombination deficiency&#8211;positive advanced ovarian cancer following response to front-line platinum-based chemotherapy (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01847274">

5299NCT01847274</a>

5300) is closed to patient accrual and results are pending.</li>

5301<li>

5302Other PARP inhibitor trials have been exploring their role in platinum-resistant disease and their role in combination with other agents. </li>

5303</ol>

5304</div>

5305</li>

5306<li>

5307Olaparib was also evaluated as a single agent in a multicenter phase II trial for patients with documented germline <em class="gene-name">

5308BRCA1</em>

5309- or <em class="gene-name">

5310BRCA2</em>

5311 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

531244</a>

5313][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5314Level of evidence C3</a>

5315] This trial was open to patients with platinum-resistant ovarian cancer, breast cancer treated with three or more previous regimens, pancreatic cancer with previously administered gemcitabine, or prostate cancer previously treated with hormonal therapy and one systemic therapy. Olaparib was given at 400 mg twice a day. The primary end point was response rate. A total of 298 patients were included. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5316<ul id="_1063">

5317<li>

5318The overall response rate was 26.2%; the response rate was 31.1% in patients with ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

531944</a>

5320][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5321Level of evidence C3</a>

5322]</li>

5323</ul>

5324</div>

5325<p id="_1064" tabindex="-1">

5326The data from this trial were used by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) to approve olaparib for patients with ovarian cancer who have known <em class="gene-name">

5327BRCA1</em>

5328 or <em class="gene-name">

5329BRCA2</em>

5330 mutations and have failed three previous regimens. </p>

5331</li>

5332<li>

5333Several other trials have combined olaparib with either cytotoxic chemotherapy or other biological therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.45">

533445</a>

5335,<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

533646</a>

5337] .<div class="pdq-content-list">

5338<ul id="_1065">

5339<li>

5340Extension in PFS, but not in OS, has been noted.</li>

5341</ul>

5342</div>

5343</li>

5344</ol>

5345</div>

5346</section>

5347</section>

5348<section id="_993">

5349<h4 id="_993_toc">

5350Platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrence</h4>

5351<section id="_339">

5352<h5 id="_339_toc">

5353Chemotherapy</h5>

5354<p id="_796" tabindex="-1">

5355Clinical recurrences that take place within 6 months of completion of a platinum-containing regimen are considered platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrences. Anthracyclines (particularly when formulated as pegylated liposomal doxorubicin), taxanes, topotecan, and gemcitabine are used as single agents for these recurrences on the basis of activity and their favorable therapeutic indices relative to agents listed in <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_343">

5356Table 10</a>

5357. The long list underscores the marginal benefit, if any, of these agents. Clinical trials should be considered for patients with platinum-resistant disease.</p>

5358<p id="_994" tabindex="-1">

5359<strong>

5360Drugs used to treat platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrences include the following:</strong>

5361</p>

5362<div class="pdq-content-list">

5363<ul id="_905">

5364<li>

5365<strong>

5366Paclitaxel.</strong>

5367 <p id="_906" tabindex="-1">

5368Treatment with paclitaxel historically provided the first agent with consistent activity in patients with platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrences.[<a href="#cit/section_7.47">

536947</a>

5370-<a href="#cit/section_7.51">

537151</a>

5372] Patients generally received paclitaxel in front-line induction regimens. Re-treatment with paclitaxel, particularly in weekly schedules, had activity comparable with that of other drugs. Residual neuropathy upon recurrence may shift the choice of treatment towards other agents.</p>

5373</li>

5374<li>

5375<strong>

5376Topotecan.</strong>

5377 <p id="_907" tabindex="-1">

5378Randomized studies have indicated that the use of topotecan achieved results that were comparable with those achieved with paclitaxel.[<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

537952</a>

5380]</p>

5381<p id="_908" tabindex="-1">

5382Evidence (topotecan):</p>

5383<div class="pdq-content-list">

5384<ol id="_909">

5385<li>

5386Topotecan was compared with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin in a randomized trial of 474 patients and demonstrated similar response rates, PFS, and OS at the time of the initial report. Responses occurred primarily in the platinum-resistant subsets.[<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

538753</a>

5388]</li>

5389<li>

5390 In phase II studies, topotecan administered intravenously (IV) on days 1 to 5 of a 21-day cycle yielded objective response rates ranging from 13% to 16.3% and other outcomes that were equivalent or superior to paclitaxel.[<a href="#cit/section_7.54">

539154</a>

5392-<a href="#cit/section_7.56">

539356</a>

5394]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5395<ul id="_962">

5396<li>

5397Objective responses were reported in patients with platinum-refractory disease.</li>

5398<li>

5399 Substantial myelosuppression followed administration. Other toxic effects included nausea, vomiting, alopecia, and asthenia. Some schedules and oral formulations to reduce toxicity are under evaluation.</li>

5400</ul>

5401</div>

5402</li>

5403<li>

5404In a phase III study, 235 patients who did not respond to initial treatment with a platinum-based regimen, but who had not previously received paclitaxel or topotecan, were randomly assigned to receive either topotecan as a 30-minute infusion daily for 5 days every 21 days or paclitaxel as a 3-hour infusion every 21 days.[<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

540552</a>

5406][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5407Level of evidence B1</a>

5408] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5409<ul id="_910">

5410<li>

5411The overall objective response rate was 20.5% for patients who were randomly assigned to treatment with topotecan and 13.2% for patients who were randomly assigned to treatment with paclitaxel (<em>

5412P</em>

5413 = .138). </li>

5414<li>

5415Both groups experienced myelosuppression and gastrointestinal (GI) toxic effects. Nausea and vomiting, fatigue, and infection were observed more commonly after treatment with topotecan, whereas alopecia, arthralgia, myalgia, and neuropathy were observed more commonly after treatment with paclitaxel.[<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

541652</a>

5417]</li>

5418</ul>

5419</div>

5420</li>

5421<li>

5422The combination of weekly topotecan and biweekly bevacizumab was evaluated in a phase II study.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5423<ul id="_911">

5424<li>

5425Results showed an objective response rate of 25% (all partial responses) in a platinum-resistant patient population.[<a href="#cit/section_7.57">

542657</a>

5427] </li>

5428<li>

5429The most common grade 3 and grade 4 toxicities were hypertension, neutropenia, and GI toxicity, although no bowel perforations occurred.</li>

5430</ul>

5431</div>

5432 </li>

5433</ol>

5434</div>

5435</li>

5436<li>

5437<strong>

5438Pegylated liposomal doxorubicin.</strong>

5439 <p id="_912" tabindex="-1">

5440Evidence (pegylated liposomal doxorubicin):</p>

5441<div class="pdq-content-list">

5442<ol id="_913">

5443<li>

5444In a phase II study encapsulated doxorubicin was given IV once every 21 to 28 days.[<a href="#cit/section_7.58">

544558</a>

5446]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5447<ul id="_914">

5448<li>

5449Results demonstrated one complete response and eight partial responses in 35 patients with platinum-refractory or paclitaxel-refractory disease (response rate, 25.7%).</li>

5450<li>

5451In general, liposomal doxorubicin has few acute side effects other than hypersensitivity. The most frequent toxic effects (stomatitis and hand-foot syndrome) were usually observed after the first cycle, and were more pronounced after dose rates exceeded 10 mg/m<span class="sup">

54522</span>

5453 per week. Neutropenia and nausea were minimal, and alopecia rarely occurred.</li>

5454</ul>

5455</div>

5456</li>

5457<li>

5458Pegylated liposomal doxorubicin and topotecan have been compared in a randomized trial of 474 patients with recurrent ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

545953</a>

5460][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5461Level of evidence A1</a>

5462]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5463<ul id="_915">

5464<li>

5465Response rates (19.7% vs. 17.0%; <em>

5466P</em>

5467 = .390), PFS (16.1 weeks vs. 17.0 weeks; <em>

5468P</em>

5469 = .095), and OS (60 weeks vs. 56.7 weeks; <em>

5470P</em>

5471 = .341) did not differ significantly between the pegylated liposomal doxorubicin and topotecan arms.[<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

547253</a>

5473][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5474Level of evidence A1</a>

5475]</li>

5476<li>

5477Survival was longer for the patients with platinum-sensitive disease who received pegylated liposomal doxorubicin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.21">

547821</a>

5479]</li>

5480</ul>

5481</div>

5482</li>

5483</ol>

5484</div>

5485 </li>

5486<li>

5487<strong>

5488Docetaxel.</strong>

5489 <p id="_916" tabindex="-1">

5490This drug has shown activity in paclitaxel-pretreated patients and is a reasonable alternative to weekly paclitaxel in the recurrent setting.[<a href="#cit/section_7.59">

549159</a>

5492]</p>

5493

5494

5495</li>

5496<li>

5497<strong>

5498Gemcitabine.</strong>

5499<p id="_1432" tabindex="-1">

5500Gemcitabine is an antimetabolite that was developed and approved in combination with platinum-based chemotherapy drugs and has shown activity as a single agent. Gemcitabine combined with cell cycle&#8722;targeted drugs and other drug combinations used in indications such as pancreatic and lung cancers are being explored.[<a href="#cit/section_7.60">

550160</a>

5502-<a href="#cit/section_7.63">

550363</a>

5504] </p>

5505<p id="_963" tabindex="-1">

5506Evidence (gemcitabine):</p>

5507<div class="pdq-content-list">

5508<ol id="_964">

5509<li>

5510Several phase II trials of gemcitabine as a single-agent&#8211;administered IV on days 1, 8, and 15 of a 28-day cycle have been reported.[<a href="#cit/section_7.60">

551160</a>

5512-<a href="#cit/section_7.62">

551362</a>

5514]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5515<ul id="_965">

5516<li>

5517The response rate ranged from 13% to 19% in evaluable patients. </li>

5518<li>

5519Responses have been observed in patients whose disease was platinum refractory and/or paclitaxel refractory as well as in patients with bulky disease.</li>

5520<li>

5521 Leukopenia, anemia, and thrombocytopenia were the most common toxic effects. Many patients reported transient flu-like symptoms and a rash after drug administration. Other toxic effects, including nausea, were usually mild.</li>

5522</ul>

5523</div>

5524</li>

5525<li>

5526A randomized trial of gemcitabine versus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin showed noninferiority and no advantage in therapeutic index of one drug over the other.[<a href="#cit/section_7.63">

552763</a>

5528]</li>

5529</ol>

5530</div>

5531</li>

5532</ul>

5533</div>

5534<div class="pdq-content-list">

5535<ul id="_934">

5536<li>

5537<strong>

5538Pemetrexed.</strong>

5539<p id="_1446" tabindex="-1">

5540Pemetrexed combined with gemcitabine has had unconvincing results compared with either agent alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.64">

554164</a>

5542,<a href="#cit/section_7.65">

554365</a>

5544] More studies are forthcoming that target cell cycle derangements common in certain genomic subtypes of ovarian cancer. Specifically, gemcitabine is presumed to be more active when there is loss of G1/S checkpoint from <em class="gene-name">

5545TP53</em>

5546 mutations, CCNE1 amplification, RB1 loss, or CDKN2A mRNA downregulation.</p>

5547<p id="_935" tabindex="-1">

5548Evidence (pemetrexed):</p>

5549<div class="pdq-content-list">

5550<ol id="_936">

5551<li>

5552A randomized, double-blinded phase II European trial with 102 patients evaluated pemetrexed at two doses: standard-dose (500 mg/m<span class="sup">

55532</span>

5554) versus high-dose (900 mg/m<span class="sup">

55552</span>

5556) IV every 3 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_7.66">

555766</a>

5558] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5559<ul id="_937">

5560<li>

5561The response rate was 9.3% for the standard dose and 10.4% for the high dose. </li>

5562<li>

5563The toxicity profile favored the standard dose, with fatigue, nausea, and vomiting as the most common severe toxicities. </li>

5564</ul>

5565</div>

5566</li>

5567<li>

5568A phase II study by the GOG utilized pemetrexed (900 mg/m<span class="sup">

55692</span>

5570) IV every 3 weeks in 51 patients with platinum-resistant recurrent disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.67">

557167</a>

5572] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5573<ul id="_938">

5574<li>

5575The response rate was 21% in a heavily pretreated population in which 39% of the patients had received five or more regimens previously. </li>

5576<li>

5577Myelosuppression and fatigue were the most common severe toxicities. </li>

5578</ul>

5579</div>

5580</li>

5581</ol>

5582</div>

5583</li>

5584</ul>

5585</div>

5586</section>

5587<section id="_1087">

5588<h5 id="_1087_toc">

5589Chemotherapy and/or bevacizumab</h5>

5590<div class="pdq-content-list">

5591<ul id="_1088">

5592<li>

5593<strong>

5594Chemotherapy with or without bevacizumab.</strong>

5595<p id="_1089" tabindex="-1">

5596The <a href="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2016/125085s317lbl.pdf" title="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2016/125085s317lbl.pdf">

5597FDA</a>

5598 has approved the use of bevacizumab in combination with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin, paclitaxel, or topotecan as a result of the OCEANS and AURELIA trials.</p>

5599<p id="_1090" tabindex="-1">

5600<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00434642">

5601OCEANS</a>

5602 (NCT00434642) assessed the role of bevacizumab in the treatment of platinum-sensitive recurrences. For more information, see the <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_957">

5603Bevacizumab, other targeted drugs, and poly (ADP-ribose) polymerase (PARP) inhibitors with or without chemotherapy</a>

5604 section.</p>

5605<p id="_1091" tabindex="-1">

5606Evidence (bevacizumab with chemotherapy):</p>

5607<div class="pdq-content-list">

5608<ol id="_1092">

5609<li>

5610The Avastin Use in Platinum-Resistant Epithelial Ovarian Cancer (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00976911">

5611AURELIA</a>

5612 [NCT00976911]) trial was an open-label, randomized trial designed to evaluate the effect of adding bevacizumab to standard chemotherapy in patients with platinum-resistant recurrent ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.68">

561368</a>

5614] Eligible patients had platinum-resistant disease (progression within 6 months of finishing a regimen) and no more than two previous regimens. Patients with platinum-refractory disease (those with progression during receipt of a platinum-containing regimen) and those with clinical or radiological signs of bowel involvement were ineligible. Patients were prescribed one of the following three chemotherapy regimens, on the basis of physician preference:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5615<ol id="_1093" class="lower-alpha">

5616<li>

5617Pegylated liposomal doxorubicin 40 mg/m<span class="sup">

56182</span>

5619 by IV on day 1 every 4 weeks.</li>

5620<li>

5621Paclitaxel 80 mg/m<span class="sup">

56222</span>

5623 by IV on days 1, 8, 15, and 22 every 4 weeks.</li>

5624<li>

5625 Topotecan 4 mg/m<span class="sup">

56262</span>

5627 by IV on days 1, 8, and 15 every 4 weeks; or 1.25 mg/m<span class="sup">

56282</span>

5629 by IV on days 1 through 5 every 3 weeks.</li>

5630</ol>

5631</div>

5632<p id="_1094" tabindex="-1">

5633Patients were then randomly assigned to receive either chemotherapy alone or chemotherapy with bevacizumab (10 mg/kg every 2 weeks, or 15 mg/kg every 3 weeks if on the 3-week-dosing schedule). Crossover to a bevacizumab-containing regimen was allowed at progression for those patients in the chemotherapy-only arm. PFS was the primary outcome, with response rate, OS, safety, and quality of life used as secondary end points. The enrollment included 361 patients with a median follow-up of 13.9 months in the chemotherapy-only arm and 13.0 months in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm. </p>

5634<div class="pdq-content-list">

5635<ul id="_1095">

5636<li>

5637Patients in the bevacizumab arm exhibited longer PFS (HR, 0.48; 95% CI, 0.38 to 0.60); median PFS was 3.4 months in the chemotherapy-alone arm versus 6.7 months in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm. </li>

5638<li>

5639The objective response rate was 12.6% in the chemotherapy-alone arm versus 30.9% in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm. </li>

5640<li>

5641There was no statistically significant difference in OS between the regimens (13.3 months chemotherapy alone vs. 16.6 months chemotherapy plus bevacizumab). </li>

5642<li>

5643Patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm had an increased incidence of hypertension and proteinuria, when compared with patients in the chemotherapy-only arm. </li>

5644<li>

5645GI perforation occurred in 2% of those receiving chemotherapy plus bevacizumab, which reflects the study&#8217;s stringent exclusion criteria.</li>

5646<li>

5647The primary end point for the quality-of-life portion of the study was a 15% or greater absolute improvement in the abdominal and GI symptom portion of the assessment modules at week 8 to week 9 of the protocol for patients in the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm.[<a href="#cit/section_7.69">

564869</a>

5649][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5650Level of evidence A3</a>

5651] The study used patient-reported outcomes from the European Organisation for Research and Treatment of Cancer Ovarian Cancer Module 28 and the Functional Assessment of Cancer Therapy-Ovarian Cancer symptom index at baseline and every 8 to 9 weeks until disease progression.</li>

5652</ul>

5653</div>

5654<p id="_1096" tabindex="-1">

5655Although there were some limitations in study design,[<a href="#cit/section_7.70">

565670</a>

5657] more patients on the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm had 15% or greater improvement in their GI scores when compared with baseline. For the chemotherapy-plus-bevacizumab arm, 34 of 115 patients (29.6%) showed improvement versus 15 of 118 (12.7%) patients who showed improvement on the chemotherapy-alone arm (difference, 16.9%; 95% CI, 6.1%&#8211;27.6%; <em>

5658P</em>

5659 = .002).</p>

5660<p id="_1097" tabindex="-1">

5661These studies confirm the effect of improving PFS when bevacizumab is added to chemotherapy for ovarian cancer. In the OCEANS trial, the HR for progression was even more prominent than in the first-line trials, and a significant effect was seen when the bevacizumab-chemotherapy combination was extended beyond six cycles until progression.</p>

5662<p id="_1098" tabindex="-1">

5663In summary, the improvement achieved by bevacizumab in relative risk and PFS rates in platinum-sensitive and platinum-resistant recurrences has been consistently more than the improvement achieved with chemotherapy alone; however, bevacizumab-related toxic effects must be considered.</p>

5664</li>

5665</ol>

5666</div>

5667</li>

5668<li>

5669<strong>

5670Bevacizumab alone.</strong>

5671<p id="_1099" tabindex="-1">

5672Three phase II studies have shown activity for this antibody to vascular endothelial growth factor.</p>

5673<div class="pdq-content-list">

5674<ol id="_1100">

5675<li>

5676The first study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00022659">

5677GOG-0170D</a>

5678) included 62 patients who had received only one or two previous treatments. These last patients had received one additional platinum-based regimen because of an initial interval of 12 months or longer after first-line regimens and also had to have a performance status of 0 or 1.[<a href="#cit/section_7.71">

567971</a>

5680] Patients received a dose of 15 mg/kg every 21 days.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5681<ul id="_1101">

5682<li>

5683There were two complete responses and 11 partial responses, a median PFS of 4.7 months, and an OS of 17 months. This activity was noted in both platinum-sensitive and platinum-resistant subsets. </li>

5684</ul>

5685</div>

5686 </li>

5687<li>

5688The second study included only patients with platinum-resistant disease using an identical dose schedule.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5689<ul id="_1102">

5690<li>

5691The study was stopped because 5 of 44 patients experienced bowel perforations, one of them fatal; seven partial responses had been observed.[<a href="#cit/section_7.72">

569272</a>

5693] This increased risk of bowel perforations was associated with three or more previous treatments.[<a href="#cit/section_7.73">

569473</a>

5695-<a href="#cit/section_7.75">

569675</a>

5697][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5698Level of evidence C2</a>

5699]</li>

5700</ul>

5701</div>

5702</li>

5703<li>

5704The third study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00072566">

5705CCC-PHII-45</a>

5706) included 70 patients who received 50 mg of oral cyclophosphamide daily, in addition to bevacizumab (10 mg/kg q 2 weeks). <div class="pdq-content-list">

5707<ul id="_1103">

5708<li>

5709Partial responses were observed in 17 patients, and 4 patients had intestinal perforations.[<a href="#cit/section_7.76">

571076</a>

5711]</li>

5712</ul>

5713</div>

5714</li>

5715</ol>

5716</div>

5717</li>

5718</ul>

5719</div>

5720</section>

5721<section id="_1464">

5722<h5 id="_1464_toc">

5723Immune checkpoint inhibitors</h5>

5724<div class="pdq-content-list">

5725<ul id="_1492">

5726<li>

5727<strong>

5728Avelumab.</strong>

5729<p id="_1478" tabindex="-1">

5730Avelumab, an antibody targeting programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1), was studied alone or in combination with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin chemotherapy followed by chemotherapy alone in patients with platinum-resistant or refractory ovarian cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_7.77">

573177</a>

5732]</p>

5733<p id="_1479" tabindex="-1">

5734Evidence (avelumab):</p>

5735<div class="pdq-content-list">

5736<ol id="_1480">

5737<li>

5738The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02580058">

5739JAVELIN Ovarian 200</a>

5740 trial (NCT02580058) accrued 556 patients between January 2016 and March 2016. Patients were randomly assigned to receive either avelumab plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin, pegylated liposomal doxorubicin alone, or avelumab alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.77">

574177</a>

5742] This study began before the FDA approved the combination of bevacizumab and pegylated liposomal doxorubicin from the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00976911">

5743AURELIA</a>

5744 trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.68">

574568</a>

5746]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5747<ul id="_1481">

5748<li>

5749The PFS and OS results failed to show superiority for avelumab over pegylated liposomal doxorubicin. The median PFS was 3.7 months (95% CI, 3.3&#8211;5.1) for patients who received the combination therapy, 3.5 months (2.1&#8211;4.0) for patients who received pegylated liposomal doxorubicin alone, and 1.9 months (1.8&#8211;1.9) for patients who received avelumab alone. The median OS was 15.7 months (95% CI, 12.7&#8211;18.7) for patients who received the combination therapy, 13.1 months (11.8&#8211;15.5) for patients who received pegylated liposomal doxorubicin alone, and 11.8 months (8.9&#8211;14.1) for patients who received avelumab alone. </li>

5750</ul>

5751</div>

5752</li>

5753</ol>

5754</div>

5755</li>

5756<li>

5757<strong>

5758Durvalumab.</strong>

5759<p id="_1483" tabindex="-1">

5760Early phase studies have evaluated the use of other immune checkpoint inhibitors (e.g., durvalumab) with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin in patients with platinum-resistant recurrent disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.78">

576178</a>

5762]</p>

5763<p id="_1484" tabindex="-1">

5764Evidence (durvalumab):</p>

5765<div class="pdq-content-list">

5766<ol id="_1485">

5767<li>

5768In a phase I/II trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02431559">

5769NCT02431559</a>

5770), published in abstract form, 40 patients scheduled to receive pegylated liposomal doxorubicin also received durvalumab.[<a href="#cit/section_7.78">

577178</a>

5772]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5773<ul id="_1486">

5774<li>

5775At 6 months, the PFS rate was 47.7% (when assessed per protocol). </li>

5776<li>

5777The OS response rate was 22.5%, with four patients achieving a complete response and five patients achieving a partial response. The median PFS was 5.5 months (0.3&#8211;28.8+) and the median OS was 17.6 months (1.7&#8211;23.5+). </li>

5778</ul>

5779</div>

5780 </li>

5781</ol>

5782</div>

5783</li>

5784</ul>

5785</div>

5786</section>

5787<section id="_1104">

5788<p id="_1106" tabindex="-1">

5789<strong>

5790Other drugs used to treat platinum-refractory or platinum-resistant recurrence (efficacy not well defined)</strong>

5791</p>

5794Table 10</a>

5796C3</a>

5797.</p>

6235 <section id="_814">

6236

6237 <h2>

6238Changes to This Summary (03/14/2023)</h2>

6239

6240 <div id="_section_814" class="pdq-sections">

6241<p id="_1449" tabindex="-1">

6242The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as new information becomes available. This section describes the latest changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

6243<p id="_1498" tabindex="-1">

6244<strong>

6245<a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_1">

6246General Information About Ovarian Epithelial Cancer, Fallopian Tube Cancer (FTC), and Primary Peritoneal Cancer (PPC)</a>

6247</strong>

6248</p>

6249<p id="_1499" tabindex="-1">

6250Updated <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_474">

6251statistics</a>

6252 with estimated new cases and deaths for 2023 (cited American Cancer Society as reference 5). </p>

6253<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

6254This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

6255PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6256, which is

6257editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

6258the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

6259information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

6260maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

6261About This PDQ Summary</a>

6262 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

6263PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

6264 pages.

6265</p>

6266</div>

6267

6268 </section>

6271

6272 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

6273

6274 <h2>

6275About This PDQ Summary</h2>

6276

6277 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

6278<section id="_AboutThis_2">

6279<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

6280Purpose of This Summary</h3>

6281<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

6282This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of ovarian epithelial, fallopian tube, and primary peritoneal cancer. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

6283</section>

6284<section id="_AboutThis_4">

6285<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

6286Reviewers and Updates</h3>

6287<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

6288This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

6289PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6290, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

6291<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

6292 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

6293<div class="pdq-content-list">

6294<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

6295<li>

6296be discussed at a meeting,</li>

6297<li>

6298be cited with text, or</li>

6299<li>

6300replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

6301</ul>

6302</div>

6303<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

6304Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

6305<p id="" tabindex="-1">

6306The lead reviewer for Ovarian Epithelial, Fallopian Tube, and Primary Peritoneal Cancer Treatment is:</p>

6307<div class="pdq-content-list">

6308<ul id="">

6309<li>

6310Olga T. Filippova, MD (Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center )</li>

6311</ul>

6312</div>

6313<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

6314Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

6315Email Us</a>

6316. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

6317</section>

6318<section id="_AboutThis_10">

6319<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

6320Levels of Evidence</h3>

6321<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

6322Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

6323formal evidence ranking system</a>

6324 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

6325</section>

6326<section id="_AboutThis_12">

6327<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

6328Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

6329<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

6330PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

6331<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

6332The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

6333<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

6334PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Ovarian Epithelial, Fallopian Tube, and Primary Peritoneal Cancer Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq">

6335https://www.cancer.gov/types/ovarian/hp/ovarian-epithelial-treatment-pdq</a>

6336. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389443]</p>

6337<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

6338Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

6339Visuals Online</a>

6340, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

6341

6342</p>

6343</section>

6344<section id="_AboutThis_17">

6345<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

6346Disclaimer</h3>

6347<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

6348Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

6349Managing Cancer Care</a>

6350 page.</p>

6351</section>

6358 page. Questions can also be submitted to Cancer.gov through the website&#8217;s <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">
